“Well, they don’t show the Dark Lord proper respect, so the name’s been **Tabooed**. A few **Order** members have been tracked that way. We’ll see. Bind them up with the other two prisoners!”

Someone yanked **Harry** up by the hair, dragged him a short way, pushed him down into a sitting position, then started binding him back-to-back with other people. **Harry** was still half blind, barely able to see anything through his puffed-up eyes. When at last the man tying then had walked away, **Harry** whispered to the other prisoners.

“Anyone still got a wand?”

“No,” said **Ron** and **Hermione** from either side of him.

“This is all my fault. I said the name. I’m sorry—”

“Harry?”

It was a new, but familiar voice, and it came from directly behind **Harry**, from the person tied to **Hermione’s** left.

“Dean?”

“It is you! If they find out who they’ve got—! They’re **Snatchers**, they’re only looking for truants to sell for gold—”

“Not a bad little haul for one night,” **Greyback** was saying, as a pair of hobnailed boots marched close by **Harry** and they heard more crashes from inside the tent. “A **Mudblood**, a runaway goblin, and these truants. You checked their names on the list yet, **Scabior**?” he roared.

“Yeah. There’s no Vernon Dudley un ’ere, **Greyback**.”

“Interesting,” said **Greyback**. “That’s interesting.”

He crouched down beside **Harry**, who saw, through the infinitesimal gap left between his swollen eyelids, a face covered in matted gray hair and whiskers, with pointed brown teeth and sores in the corners of his mouth. **Greyback** smelled as he had done at the top of the tower where **Dumbledore** had died: of dirt, sweat, and blood.

“So you aren’t wanted, then, Vernon? Or are you on that list under a different name? What house were you in at **Hogwarts**?”

“**Slytherin**,” said **Harry** automatically.

“Funny ’ow they all thinks we wants to ’ear that,” leered **Scabior** out of the shadows. “But none of ’em can tell us where the common room is.”

“It’s in the dungeons,” said **Harry** clearly. “You enter through the wall. It’s full of skulls and stuff and its under the lake, so the light’s all green.”

There was a short pause.

“Well, well, looks like we really ’ave caught a little **Slytherin**,” said **Scabior**. “Good for you, Vernon, ’cause there ain’t a lot of **Mudblood Slytherins**. Who’s your father?”

“He works at the **Ministry**,” **Harry** lied. He knew that his whole story would collapse with the smallest investigation, but on the other hand, he only had until his face regained its usual appearance before the game was up in any case. “Department of Magical Accidents and Catastrophes.”

“You know what, **Greyback**,” said **Scabior**. “I think there is a Dudley in there.”

**Harry** could barely breathe: Could luck, sheer luck, get them safely out of this?

“Well, well,” said **Greyback**, and **Harry** could hear the tiniest note of trepidation in that callous voice, and knew that **Greyback** was wondering whether he had just indeed just attacked and bound the son of a **Ministry Official**. **Harry’s** heart was pounding against the ropes around his ribs; he would not have been surprised to know that **Greyback** could see it. “If you’re telling the truth, ugly, you’ve got nothing to fear from a trip to the **Ministry**. I expect your father’ll reward us just for picking you up.”

“But,” said **Harry**, his mouth bone dry, “if you just let us—”

“Hey!” came a shout from inside the tent. “Look at this, **Greyback**!”

## Capture of Harry Potter

A **dark figure** came bustling toward them, and **Harry** saw a glint of **silver** to the light of their wands. They had found **Gryffindor’s sword**.

“Ve-e-ery nice,” said **Greyback** appreciatively, taking it from his companion. “Oh, very nice indeed. Looks **goblin-made**, that. Where did you get something like this?”

“It’s my father’s,” **Harry** lied, hoping against hope that it was too dark for Greyback to see the name etched just below the hilt. “We borrowed it to cut firewood—”

“’Ang on a minute, Greyback! Look at this, in the Prophet!”

## Harry’s Scar and Voldemort’s Thoughts

As **Scabior** said it, **Harry’s scar**, which was stretched tight across his distended forehead, burned savagely. More clearly than he could make out anything around him, he saw a towering building, a grim fortress, jet-black and forbidding: **Voldemort’s thoughts** had suddenly become razor-sharp again; he was gliding toward the gigantic building with a sense of calmly euphoric purpose…

So close… So close… With a huge effort of will, **Harry closed his mind** to Voldemort’s thoughts, pulling himself back to where he sat, tied to **Ron, Hermione, Dean, and Griphook** in the darkness, listening to Greyback and Scabior.

## Identification of the Prisoners

“‘**Hermione Granger**,’” Scabior was saying, “‘the **Mudblood** who is known to be traveling with ’Arry Potter.’”

Harry’s scar burned in the silence, but he made a supreme effort to keep himself present, nor to slip into Voldemort’s mind. He heard the creak of Greyback’s boots as he crouched down, in front of Hermione.

“You know what, little girly? This picture looks a hell of a lot like you.”

“It isn’t! It isn’t me!”

Hermione’s terrified squeak was as good as a confession.

“‘…known to be traveling with Harry Potter,’” repeated Greyback quietly.

A stillness had settled over the scene. Harry’s scar was exquisitely painful, but he struggled with all his strength against the pull of Voldemort’s thoughts. It had never been so important to remain in his own right mind.

## Greyback Examines Harry

“Well, this changed things, doesn’t it?” whispered Greyback. Nobody spoke: Harry sensed the gang of **Snatchers** watching, frozen, and felt Hermione’s arm trembling against his. Greyback got up and took a couple of steps to where Harry sat, crouching down again to stare closely at his misshapen features.

“What’s that on your forehead, **Vernon**?” he asked softly, his breath foul in Harry’s nostrils as he pressed a filthy finger to the taut scar.

“Don’t touch it!” Harry

## Malfoy Manor: The Capture of Potter and Friends

### Suspicion and Identification

- **Narcissa Malfoy** expresses caution about being certain it is **Harry Potter** before summoning the **Dark Lord**.
- She inspects a **blackthorn wand** but notes it does not match **Ollivander's description**.
- **Greyback** questions the identity of the **Mudblood**, soon identified as **Hermione Granger**.
- **Lucius Malfoy** and **Draco Malfoy** recognize **Ron Weasley** among the prisoners.
- **Bellatrix Lestrange** arrives, confirming the identities of **Potter, Granger, and Weasley**.

### The Conflict Over Authority

- **Lucius** intends to summon the **Dark Lord** using his authority.
- **Bellatrix** challenges Lucius’s authority after he lost his wand.
- **Greyback** asserts that his group captured Potter and claims the reward.
- Bellatrix dismisses the reward, seeking only honor in serving the **Dark Lord**.

### The Dark Mark and Danger

- Bellatrix and Lucius hesitate to touch their **Dark Marks** fearing a dangerous summoning.
- An argument ensues about the risk of summoning the **Dark Lord** prematurely.
- Bellatrix instructs to place the prisoners in the **cellar** for safety and further planning.

### Bellatrix’s Unexpected Discovery

- Bellatrix examines a **sword of Gryffindor** found with the prisoners, sent to her vault by **Severus Snape**.
- She questions **Greyback** about how the sword was obtained.
- The sword's presence causes alarm among the Death Eaters.

### Treatment of the Prisoners

- Bellatrix orders all prisoners except **Hermione** to be taken to the cellar.
- She threatens Ron and declares him a **blood traitor**.
- **Greyback** forces the prisoners down to the cellar with his wand projecting an invisible force.

### The Prisoners in the Cellar

- Harry, Ron, and others are tied back-to-back in a dark, damp cellar.
- Hermione’s desperate screams echo from above as Bellatrix interrogates her.
- Ron tries to protect Hermione, receiving a harsh blow from Bellatrix.

### Luna’s Rescue Efforts

- **Luna Lovegood** secretly arrives to help the prisoners.
- She uses an old **nail** to start freeing their ropes.
- **Mr. Ollivander** assists Luna while remaining weak and injured.
- Ron uses his **Deluminator** to provide light in the otherwise dark cellar.

### Struggle and Desperation

- Bellatrix continues to torture Hermione upstairs.
- Ron tries to find an escape but the cellar is magically secured.
- Harry desperately searches the cellar walls for any means of escape.
- He uses objects from **Hagrid’s pouch**, including **Dumbledore’s Snitch** and a **fragment of the phoenix wand mirror**.

### Dumbledore’s Eye and Final Cry for Help

- Through the mirror shard, Harry briefly sees **Dumbledore’s eye**.
- He calls out for help, but the vision blinks away.
- Hermione’s screams and Ron’s calls fill the cellar with despair.
- Bellatrix accuses the goblin **Griphook** of aiding the prisoners in breaking into her vault.

## Scene: The Vault and the Cellar Confrontation

“We only met him **tonight**!” **Hermione** sobbed. “We’ve never been inside your vault… It isn’t the real sword! It’s a **copy**, just a copy!”

“A **copy**?” screeched **Bellatrix**. “Oh, a likely story!”

“But we can find out easily!” came **Lucius**’s voice. “**Draco**, fetch the goblin, he can tell us whether the sword is real or not!”

**Harry** dashed across the cellar to where **Griphook** was huddled on the floor.

“Griphook,” he whispered into the goblin’s pointed ear, “you must tell them that sword’s a **fake**, they mustn’t know it’s the real one, Griphook, please—”

He could hear someone scuttling down the cellar steps; next moment, **Draco**’s shaking voice spoke

## Harry’s Scar and the Escape

**Harry’s scar** was blinding him with pain. Dimly he knew that they had moments, seconds before **Voldemort** was with them.

- “Ron, catch—and GO!” he yelled, throwing one of the **wands** to him.
- He bent down to tug **Griphook** out from under the chandelier.
- Hoisting the groaning goblin, who still clung to the sword, over one shoulder, Harry seized **Dobby’s** hand.
- He spun on the spot to **Disapparate**.

As he turned into darkness he caught one last view of the drawing room of the pale, frozen figures of **Narcissa** and **Draco**, of the streak of red that was Ron’s hair, and a blue of flying silver, as **Bellatrix’s knife** flew across the room at the place where he was vanishing—

## Arrival at Shell Cottage

**Bill and Fleur’s Shell Cottage** appeared under the wide starry sky. Harry fell to his knees, relinquished **Dobby’s hand**, and gently lowered **Griphook** to the ground after Disapparating.

- Harry squinted through the darkness.
- Movement was seen outside the cottage.
- Harry whispered, “Dobby, is this Shell Cottage? Have we come to the right place?”

The elf stood feet from him.

Suddenly, **Dobby** swayed with a silver knife protruding from his heaving chest.

- Harry bellowed, “HELP!”
- The dark stain was spreading as the elf stretched out his arms to Harry.
- Harry caught him and laid him sideways on the cool grass.
- “Dobby, no, don’t die, don’t die—”
- The elf’s lips trembled with the effort to form words: “Harry… Potter…”
- Then Dobby became quite still, his eyes glassy orbs sprinkled with starlight.

---

## 24. THE WANDMAKER

Harry knelt again beside Dobby’s body, pierced by **Bellatrix’s silver knife**. His voice repeatedly said, “Dobby… Dobby…” knowing the elf had gone.

- Bill, Fleur, Dean, and Luna gathered.
- Hermione had been taken inside by Ron and was expected to be all right.
- Harry pulled the sharp blade from Dobby’s body.
- He covered Dobby with his jacket like a blanket.

The sea’s rush was nearby. Others were making decisions while Dean carried injured Griphook inside, Fleur hurrying with them.

- Harry’s scar prickled; he felt Voldemort punishing those left behind at **Malfoy Manor**.
- His grief for Dobby diminished the rage, making it a distant storm.

---

## Harry’s Burial of Dobby

“I want to do it properly. Not by magic. Have you got a spade?” Harry said.

- He dug the grave alone, furious yet relishing the manual labor.
- Every drop of sweat and blister felt like a gift to the elf who saved their lives.
- Harry’s scar burned, but he controlled the pain.
- He had learned to shut his mind to Voldemort — a lesson from **Dumbledore** and **Snape**.
- Grief drove Voldemort out, or as Dumbledore might say, it was **love**.

As he dug deeper, memories and understanding came:

- Thoughts of **Hallows** and **Horcruxes** came clearly.
- He knew where Voldemort had been, whom he had killed in **Nurmengard** and why.
- He thought of **Wormtail**, dead due to a small impulse of mercy foreseen by Dumbledore.

After some time, **Ron** and **Dean** joined him.

- Hermione was better, cared for by Fleur.
- They worked in silence to deepen the grave.

Harry wrapped Dobby more securely, while Ron put on the elf’s shoes and socks, and Dean placed a woolen hat on Dobby’s head. Luna gently closed the elf’s eyes, saying, “Now he could be sleeping.”

---

## The Farewell

Harry placed Dobby into the grave, arranging his limbs as if resting.

- He remembered Dumbledore’s grand funeral with rows of golden chairs and the **Minister of Magic**.
- Dobby deserved a grand funeral as well, but lay in a roughly dug hole between bushes.

Luna spoke first, addressing Dobby:

> “Thank you so much, Dobby, for rescuing me from that cellar. It’s so unfair that you had to die when you were so good and brave. I’ll always remember what you did for us. I hope you’re happy now.”

Others followed:

- Ron: “Yeah… thanks, Dobby.”
- Dean: “Thanks.”
- Harry: “Goodbye, Dobby.”

Bill raised his wand; earth rose and covered the grave, forming a small reddish mound.

Bill asked, “D’ya mind if I stay here a moment?” They murmured words, patted Harry’s back, and went back to the cottage, leaving Harry alone.

Harry picked up a large, smooth white stone and laid it over Dobby’s head.

- He used his wand to inscribe on the stone:

  **HERE LIES DOBBY, A FREE ELF.**

---

## At Shell Cottage After the Burial

Harry entered the living room where Bill was speaking.

- The room was light-colored and pretty, with a small fire burning in the fireplace.
- Bill said, “Lucky Ginny’s on holiday. If she’d been at Hogwarts, they could have taken her before reaching her. We’ve moved the family to Muriel’s for protection.”
- Bill explained the **Fidelius Charm** was in place, with his dad as Secret-Keeper.
- The same charm protects the cottage; Bill is Secret-Keeper here.
- Griphook’s legs were healing with **Skele-Gro**.
- Bill wanted to move everyone to Muriel’s once they recovered.

Harry insisted:

- “No. I need both of them here. I need to talk to them. It’s important.”
- His voice carried authority and conviction gained while digging Dobby’s grave.

All looked puzzled.

Harry announced he was going to wash and asked to see them straight away.

## Harry's Morning Reflection

He walked into the little kitchen, to the basin beneath a window overlooking the sea. **Dawn** was breaking over the horizon, shell pink and faintly gold, as he washed, again following the train of thought that had come to him in the dark garden.

**Dobby** would never be able to tell them who had sent him to the cellar, but **Harry** knew what he had seen. A piercing blue eye had looked out of the mirror fragment, and then help had come. **Help will always be given at Hogwarts to those who ask for it.**

Harry dried his hands, impervious to the beauty of the scene outside and to the murmuring others in the sitting room. He felt closer than ever before, closer to the heart of it all.

His **scar prickled**, and he knew that **Voldemort** was getting there too. Harry understood and yet did not understand. His instinct told him one thing, his brain another. The **Dumbledore** in Harry’s head smiled, surveying him over the tips of his fingers, pressed as if in prayer.

- You gave Ron the **Deluminator**… You understood him… You gave him a way back…
- And you understood **Wormtail** too… You knew there was a bit of regret there…
- And if you knew them… What did you know about me, **Dumbledore**?
- Am I meant to know but not to seek?
- Did you know how hard I’d feel that?
- Is that why you made it this difficult? So I’d have time to work that out?

Harry stood still, eyes glazed, watching a bright gold ray of dazzling sun rise over the horizon. He looked down at his clean hands and was momentarily surprised to see the cloth he was holding. He set it down and returned to the hall. His scar pulsed angrily, then flashed in his mind the outline of a building he knew extremely well.

---

## Encounter with Bill and Fleur

**Bill** and **Fleur** were standing at the foot of the stairs.

- Harry: “I need to speak to **Griphook** and **Ollivander**.”
- Fleur: “No, you will ’ave to wait, ‘Arry. Zey are both too tired—”
- Harry, firm: “I’m sorry, but it can’t wait. I need to talk to them privately—and separately. It’s urgent.”

Bill was confused and angry.

- Bill: “You turn up here with a dead house-elf and a half-conscious goblin, **Hermione** looks tortured, and **Ron** won’t tell me anything.”
- Harry: “We can’t tell you what we’re doing. You’re in the **Order**, Bill. Dumbledore left us a mission. We’re not supposed to talk about it to anyone else.”

Bill agreed reluctantly.

- Bill: “All right. Who do you want to talk to first?”
- Harry: “Griphook. I’ll speak to **Griphook** first.”

Harry’s heart raced as if after sprinting.

- Bill leads: “Up here, then.”

---

## Meeting with Griphook

Harry stopped and called for Ron and Hermione to join them.

- Harry: “I need you two as well!”
- Ron and Hermione emerged, looking relieved.
- Harry praised Hermione: “You were amazing, coming up with that story when she was hurting you.”

Ron asked, “What are we doing now, Harry?”

- Harry: “You’ll see. Come on.”

They followed Bill upstairs onto a small landing with three doors.

- Bill opened the door to his and Fleur’s room, overlooking the sea.

Harry stood by the window with his arms folded, scar prickling. Hermione sat beside the dressing table; Ron on the arm of the chair.

Bill returned carrying the little goblin and set him on the bed.

- Griphook grunted thanks.
- Bill left, closing the door.

Harry apologized for waking Griphook and asked about his legs.

- Griphook: “Painful, but mending.”
- He still clutched the **Sword of Gryffindor**, looking half truculent, half intrigued.

Harry noted the goblin’s:

- Sallow skin
- Long thin fingers
- Black eyes
- Dirty long feet
- Domed head much bigger than a human’s

---

## Conversation with Griphook

- Griphook: “I was the goblin who showed you to your vault the first time at **Gringotts**. You are very famous, Harry Potter.”

The scar still prickled. Harry wanted to act carefully.

- Griphook: “You buried the elf. I watched from the window next door.”
- Harry: “Yes.”
- Griphook: “You are an unusual wizard.”
- Harry: “In what way?”
- Griphook: “You dug the grave.”
- Harry: “So?”
- Griphook did not respond; his look seemed to sneer at Harry’s Muggle-like action.

Harry gathered courage.

- Harry: “I need to ask you something.”
- Griphook: “You also rescued a goblin.”
- Harry, surprised: “What?”
- Griphook: “You brought me here. Saved me.”
- Harry: “Well, I take it you’re not sorry?”
- Griphook: “No, Harry Potter, but you are a very odd wizard.”

---

## Request for Help

- Harry: “I need some help, Griphook. You can give it to me.”
- Griphook frowned, unconvinced.
- Harry: “I need to break into a Gringotts vault.”
- The words were forced from him as pain shot through his scar.

Ron and Hermione stared at Harry as if mad.

- Hermione began to protest but was cut off.
- Griphook: “Break into a Gringotts vault? Impossible.”
- Ron: “It’s been done.”
- Harry: “The same day I first met you, Griphook. My birthday, seven years ago.”
- Griphook: “That vault was empty then, protection minimal.”
- Harry: “The vault we need isn’t empty; its protection will be powerful. It belongs to the **Lestranges**.”

Hermione and Ron looked astonished.

- Griphook: “You have no chance. If you seek beneath our floors a treasure never yours—”
- Harry: “Thief, you have been warned, beware—I know. But I’m not after treasure or personal gain.”
  
Griphook looked slantwise at Harry; the scar prickled but Harry ignored it.

- Griphook: “If there was a wizard not seeking gain, it would be you, Harry Potter.”
- “Goblins and elves aren't used to the protection and respect you have shown this night. Not from wand-carriers.”

Harry repeated the phrase "wand-carriers" as his scar prickled and Voldemort’s thoughts turned north.

- Griphook: “The right to carry a wand has long been contested between wizards and goblins.”
- Ron: “Goblins can do magic without wands.”
- Griphook: “Immaterial! Wizards refuse to share wand-lore.”
- Ron: “Goblins won’t share their magic either; they know how to work metal like swords and armor.”

Harry interrupted:

- “This isn’t about wizards vs goblins or other magical creatures.”

Griphook laughed nastily.

- “But it is precisely that! As the **Dark Lord** grows stronger, your race is set above mine! Gringotts falls under wizarding rule, house-elves are slaughtered, and who protests?”
- Hermione: “We do! I’m hunted as much as any goblin or elf. I’m a **Mudblood**!”
- Ron muttered “Don’t call yourself—”
- Hermione: “Why shouldn’t I? Mudblood, and proud! I have no better position than you under this new order! It was me they tortured at the Malfoys’.”
- She revealed a thin scar on her throat made by Bellatrix.

---

## Plea for Assistance

- Hermione asked if Griphook knew it was Harry who set Dobby free.
- She mentioned their desire to free elves for years.
- Ron fidgeted uncomfortably.

Griphook gazed at Hermione with curiousity.

- Griphook: “What do you seek in the Lestranges’ vault?”
- “The sword inside is a fake. This is the real one.”
- He looked at them and said, “I think you know. You asked me to lie for you.”

Harry pressed on:

- “The fake sword isn’t the only thing in that vault.”
- “Perhaps you’ve seen other things?”

His heart pounded; the scar pulsed again.

- The goblin twisted his beard.
- “It’s against our code to speak of Gringotts’ secrets. We are guardians of fabulous treasures, wrought by our fingers.”
- The goblin stroked the sword, eyes moving among them.
- “So young to be fighting so many.”

Harry asked:

- “Will you help us? We need your help to break in. You’re our only chance.”

Griphook answered maddeningly:

- “I shall… think about it.”

Ron started angrily but was nudged by Hermione.

Harry thanked him.

- The goblin bowed his domed head in acknowledgment and flexed his legs.
- “I think **Skele-Gro** has finished its work. I may sleep at last. Forgive me…”

## Conversation About the Sword of Gryffindor and the Lestranges Vault

“**Yeah, of course,**” said **Harry**, but before leaving the room he leaned forward and took the **sword of Gryffindor** from beside the goblin. **Griphook** did not protest, but Harry thought he saw resentment in the goblin’s eyes as he closed the door upon him.

“**Little git,**” whispered **Ron**. “He’s enjoying keeping us hanging.”

“**Harry,**” whispered **Hermione**, pulling them both away from the door, into the middle of the still-dark landing, “are you saying what I think you’re saying? Are you saying there’s a **Horcrux** in the **Lestranges vault**?”

“Yes,” said **Harry**. “**Bellatrix** was terrified when she thought we’d been in there, she was beside herself. Why? What did she think we’d seen, what else did she think we might have taken? Something she was petrified **You-Know-Who** would find out about.”

“But I thought we were looking for places **You-Know-Who’s** been, places he’s done something important?” said **Ron**, looking baffled. “Was he ever inside the **Lestranges’ vault**?”

“I don’t know whether he was ever inside **Gringotts,**” said **Harry**. “He never had gold there when he was younger, because nobody left him anything. He would have seen the bank from the outside, though, the first time he ever went to **Diagon Alley.**”

Harry’s **scar** throbbed, but he ignored it; he wanted Ron and Hermione to understand about **Gringotts** before they spoke to **Ollivander.**

“I think he would have envied anyone who had a key to a **Gringotts vault**. I think he’d have seen it as a real symbol of belonging to the **Wizarding world**. And don’t forget, he trusted **Bellatrix** and her husband. They were his most devoted servants before he fell, and they went looking for him after he vanished. He said it night he came back, I heard him.”

Harry rubbed his **scar**.

“I don’t think he’d have told Bellatrix it was a **Horcrux,** though. He never told **Lucius Malfoy** the truth about the diary. He probably told her it was a treasured possession and asked her to place it in her vault. The safest place in the world for anything you want to hide, **Hagrid** told me… except for **Hogwarts.**”

When Harry had finished speaking, Ron shook his head.

“You really understand him.”

“Bits of him,” said Harry. “Bits… I just wish I’d understood **Dumbledore** as much. But we’ll see. Come on—**Ollivander** now.”

## Visiting Ollivander

Ron and Hermione looked bewildered but very impressed as they followed him across the little landing and knocked upon the door opposite **Bill** and **Fleur’s.** A weak “Come in!” answered them.

The wandmaker was lying on the twin bed farthest from the window. He had been held in the cellar for more than a year, and tortured, Harry knew, on at least one occasion. He was emaciated, the bones of his face sticking out sharply against the yellowish skin. His great silver eyes seemed vast in their sunken sockets. The hands that lay upon the blanket could have belonged to a skeleton. Harry sat down on the empty bed, beside Ron and Hermione. The rising sun was not visible here. The room faced the cliff-top garden and the freshly dug grave.

“**Mr. Ollivander, I’m sorry to disturb you,**” Harry said.

“**My dear boy,**” Ollivander’s voice was feeble. “You rescued us, I thought we would die in that place, I can never thank you… never thank you… enough.”

“We were glad to do it.”

Harry’s **scar** throbbed. He knew, he was certain, that there was hardly any time left in which to beat **Voldemort** to his goal, or else to attempt to thwart him. He felt a flutter of panic… yet he had made his decision when he chose to speak to **Griphook** first. Feigning a calm he did not feel, he groped in the pouch around his neck and took out the two halves of his broken wand.

“**Mr. Ollivander, I need some help.**”

“Anything. Anything,” said the wandmaker weakly.

“**Can you mend this? Is it possible?**”

Ollivander held out a trembling hand, and Harry placed the two barely connected halves in his palm.

“**Holly and phoenix feather,**” said Ollivander in a tremulous voice. “Eleven inches. Nice and supple.”

“Yes,” said Harry. “**Can you—?**”

“No,” whispered Ollivander. “I am sorry, very sorry, but a wand that has suffered this degree of damage cannot be repaired by any means that I know of.”

Harry had been braced to hear it, but it was a blow nevertheless. He took the wand halves back and replaced them in the pouch around his neck. Ollivander stared at the place where the shattered wand had vanished, and did not look away until Harry had taken from his pocket the two wands he had brought from the Malfoys’.

“**Can you identify these?**” Harry asked.

The wandmaker took the first of the wands and held it close to his faded eyes, rolling it between his knobbly-knuckled fingers, flexing it slightly.

“**Walnut and dragon heartstring,**” he said. “Twelve-and-three-quarter inches. Unyielding. This wand

## Elder Wand and Deathly Hallows Discussion

“Never mind how I know it,” said **Harry**, closing his eyes momentarily as his scar burned and he saw, for mere seconds, a vision of the main street in **Hogsmeade**, still dark, because it was so much farther north. “You told **You-Know-Who** that **Gregorovitch** had the wand?”

“It was a rumor,” whispered **Ollivander**. “A rumor, years and years ago, long before you were born, I believe Gregorovitch himself started it. You can see how good it would be for business; that he was studying and duplicating the qualities of the **Elder Wand**!”

“Yes, I can see that,” said Harry. He stood up. “Mr. Ollivander, one last thing, and then we’ll let you get some rest. What do you know about the **Deathly Hallows**?”

“The—the what?” asked the wandmaker, looking utterly bewildered.

“The **Deathly Hallows**.”

“I’m afraid I don’t know what you’re talking about. Is this still something to do with **wands**?”

Harry looked into the sunken face and believed that Ollivander was not acting. He did not know about the **Hallows**.

“Thank you,” said Harry. “Thank you very much. We’ll leave you to get some rest now.”

Ollivander looked stricken.

“He was torturing me!” he gasped. “The **Cruciatus Curse**… you have no idea…”

“I do,” said Harry, “I really do. Please get some rest. Thank you for telling me all of this.”

He led **Ron** and **Hermione** down the staircase. Harry caught glimpses of **Bill**, **Fleur**, **Luna**, and **Dean** sitting at the table in the kitchen, cups of tea in front of them. They all looked up at Harry as he appeared in the doorway, but he merely nodded to them and continued into the garden, Ron and Hermione behind him. The reddish mound of earth that covered **Dobby** lay ahead, and Harry walked back to it, as the pain in his head built more and more powerfully. It was a huge effort now to close down the visions that were forcing themselves upon him, but he knew that he would have to resist only a little longer. He would yield very soon, because he needed to know that his theory was right. He must make only one more short effort, so that he could explain to Ron and Hermione.

“Gregorovitch had the **Elder Wand** a long time ago,” he said, “I saw **You-Know-Who** trying to find him. When he tracked him down, he found that Gregorovitch didn’t have it anymore: It was stolen from him by **Grindelwald**. How Grindelwald found out that Gregorovitch had it, I don’t know—but if Gregorovitch was stupid enough to spread the rumor, it can’t have been that difficult.”

**Voldemort** was at the gates of **Hogwarts**; Harry could see him standing there, and see too the lamp bobbing in the pre-dawn, coming closer and closer.

“And Grindelwald used the **Elder Wand** to become powerful. And at the height of his power, when **Dumbledore** knew he was the only one who could stop him, he dueled Grindelwald and beat him, and he took the **Elder Wand**.”

“Dumbledore had the **Elder Wand**?” said Ron. “But then—where is it now?”

“At Hogwarts,” said Harry, fighting to remain with them in the cliff-top garden.

“But then, let’s go!” said Ron urgently. “Harry, let’s go and get it before he does!”

“It’s too late for that,” said Harry. He could not help himself, but clutched his head, trying to help it resist. “He knows where it is. He’s there now.”

“Harry!” Ron said furiously. “How long have you known this—why have we been wasting time? Why did you talk to **Griphook** first? We could have gone—we could still go—”

“No,” said Harry, and he sank to his knees in the grass. “Hermione’s right. Dumbledore didn’t want me to have it. He didn’t want me to take it. He wanted me to get the **Horcruxes**.”

“The unbeatable wand, Harry!” moaned Ron.

“I’m not supposed to… I’m supposed to get the **Horcruxes**…”

## Securing the Elder Wand at Hogwarts

And now everything was cool and dark: The sun was barely visible over the horizon as he glided alongside **Snape**, up through the grounds toward the lake.

“I shall join you in the castle shortly,” he said in his high, cold voice. “Leave me now.”

Snape bowed and set off back up the path, his black cloak billowing behind him. Harry walked slowly, waiting for Snape’s figure to disappear. It would not do for Snape, or indeed anyone else, to see where he was going. But there were no lights in the castle windows, and he could conceal himself… and in a second he had cast upon himself a **Disillusionment Charm** that hid him even from his own eyes.

And he walked on, around the edge of the lake, taking in the outlines of the beloved castle, his first kingdom, his birthright…

And here it was, beside the lake, reflected in the dark waters. The **white marble tomb**, an unnecessary blot on the familiar landscape. He felt again that rush of controlled euphoria, that heady sense of purpose in destruction. He raised the old **yew wand**: How fitting that this would be its last great act.

The tomb split open from head to foot. The shrouded figure was as long and thin as it had been in life. He raised the wand again.

The wrappings fell open. The face was translucent, pale, sunken, yet almost perfectly preserved. They had left his spectacles on the crooked nose: He felt amused derision. **Dumbledore’s** hands were folded upon his chest, and there it lay, clutched beneath them, buried with him.

Had the old fool imagined that marble or death would protect the wand? Had he thought that the Dark Lord would be scared to violate his tomb? The spiderlike hand swooped and pulled the wand from Dumbledore’s grasp, and as he took it, a shower of sparks flew from its tip, sparkling over the corpse of its last owner, ready to serve a new master at last.

## 25. Shell Cottage

**Bill** and **Fleur’s** cottage stood alone on a cliff overlooking the sea, its walls embedded with shells and whitewashed. It was a lonely and beautiful place. Wherever Harry went inside the tiny cottage or its garden, he could hear the constant ebb and flow of the sea, like the breathing of some great, slumbering creature. 

He spent much of the next few days making excuses to escape the crowded cottage, craving the cliff-top view of open sky and wide, empty sea, and the feel of cold, salty wind on his face. The enormity of his decision not to race Voldemort to the wand still scared Harry. He could not remember, ever before, choosing not to act. He was full of doubts, doubts that Ron could not help voicing whenever they were together.

- “What if Dumbledore wanted us to work out the symbol in time to get the wand?”
- “What if working out what the symbol meant made you ‘worthy’ to get the Hallows?”
- “Harry, if that really is the Elder Wand, how the hell are we supposed to finish off You-Know-Who?”

Harry had no answers: There were moments when he wondered whether it had been outright madness not to try to prevent Voldemort breaking open the tomb. He could not even explain satisfactorily why he had decided against it: Every time he tried to reconstruct the internal arguments that had led to his decision, they sounded feebler to him.

The odd thing was that Hermione’s support made him feel just as confused as Ron’s doubts. Now forced to accept that the **Elder Wand** was real, she maintained that it was an **evil object**, and that the way Voldemort had taken possession of it was repellent, not to be considered.

“You could never have done that, Harry,” she said again and again. “You couldn’t have broken into Dumbledore’s grave.”

But the idea of **Dumbledore’s corpse** frightened Harry much less than the possibility that he might have misunderstood the living Dumbledore’s intentions. He felt that he was still groping in the dark; he had chosen his path but kept looking back, wondering whether he had misread the signs, whether he should not have taken the other way. From time to time, anger at Dumbledore crashed over him again, powerful as the waves slamming themselves against the cliff beneath the cottage, anger that Dumbledore had not explained before he died.

“But is he dead?” said Ron, three days after they had arrived at the cottage. Harry had been staring out over the wall that separated the cottage garden from the cliff when Ron and Hermione had found him; he wished they had not, having no wish to join in with their argument.

“Yes, he is. Ron, please don’t start that again!”

“Look at the facts, Hermione,” said Ron, speaking across Harry, who continued to gaze at the horizon. “The **silver doe

## Goblins, Wizards, and the Sword of Gryffindor

“I don’t know,” she said hopelessly. **“Wizarding history** often skates over what the **wizards have done to other magical races

## Arrival of Remus Lupin

“Who is it?” **Bill** called.

“It is I, **Remus John Lupin**!” called a voice over the howling wind. **Harry** experienced a thrill of fear; what had happened? “I am a **werewolf**, married to **Nymphadora Tonks**, and you, the **Secret-Keeper of Shell Cottage**, told me the address and bade me come in an emergency!”

“Lupin,” muttered **Bill**, and he ran to the door and wrenched it open.

Lupin fell over the threshold. He was white-faced, wrapped in a traveling cloak, his graying hair windswept. He straightened up, looked around the room, making sure of who was there, then cried aloud, “It’s a boy! We’ve named him **Ted**, after Dora’s father!”

**Hermione** shrieked.

“Wha—? Tonks—Tonks has had the baby?”

“Yes, yes, she’s had the baby!” shouted **Lupin**. All around the table came cries of delight, sighs of relief: **Hermione** and **Fleur** both squealed, “Congratulations!” and **Ron** said, “Blimey, a baby!” as if he had never heard of such a thing before.

“Yes—yes—a boy,” said **Lupin** again, who seemed dazed by his own happiness. He strode around the table and hugged **Harry**; the scene in the basement of **Grimmauld Place** might never have happened.

“You’ll be godfather?” he said as he released **Harry**.

“M-me?” stammered **Harry**.

“You, yes, of course—Dora quite agrees, no one better—”

“I—yeah—blimey—”

**Harry** felt overwhelmed, astonished, delighted; now **Bill** was hurrying to fetch wine, and **Fleur** was persuading **Lupin** to join them for a drink.

“I can’t stay long, I must get back,” said **Lupin**, beaming around at them all: He looked years younger than **Harry** had ever seen him. “Thank you, thank you, Bill—”

**Bill** had soon filled all of their goblets, they stood and raised them high in a toast.

“To **Teddy Remus Lupin**,” said **Lupin**, “a great wizard in the making!”

“’Oo does ’e look like?” **Fleur** inquired.

“I think he looks like **Dora**, but she thinks he is like me. Not much hair. It looked **black** when he was born, but I swear it’s turned **ginger** in the hour since. Probably **blond** by the time I get back. **Andromeda** says Tonks’s hair started changing color the day that she was born.” He drained his goblet. “Oh, go on then, just one more,” he added, beaming, as **Bill** made to fill it again.

The wind buffeted the little cottage and the fire leapt and crackled, and **Bill** was soon opening another bottle of wine. **Lupin’s** news seemed to have taken them out of themselves, removed them for a while from their state of siege: Tidings of new life were exhilarating. Only the goblin seemed untouched by the suddenly festive atmosphere, and after a while he slunk back to the bedroom he now occupied alone. **Harry** thought he was the only one who had noticed this, until he saw **Bill’s** eyes following the goblin up the stairs.

“No… no… I really must get back,” said **Lupin** at last, declining yet another goblet of wine. He got to his feet and pulled his traveling cloak back around himself.

“Good-bye, good-bye—I’ll try and bring some pictures in a few day’s time—they’ll all be so glad to know that I’ve seen you—”

He fastened his cloak and made his farewells, hugging the women and grasping hands with the men, then, still beaming, returned into the wild night.

“Godfather, Harry!” said **Bill** as they walked into the kitchen together, helping clear the table. “A real honor! Congratulations!”

As **Harry** set down the empty goblets he was carrying, **Bill** pulled the door behind him closed, shutting out the still-voluble voices of the others, who were continuing to celebrate even in **Lupin’s** absence.

## Bill's Warning About Goblins

“I wanted a private word, actually, **Harry**. It hasn’t been easy to get an opportunity with the cottage this full of people.” **Bill** hesitated. “**Harry**, you’re planning something with **Griphook**.”

It was a statement, not a question, and **Harry** did not bother to deny it. He merely looked at **Bill**, waiting.

“I know goblins,” said **Bill**. “I’ve worked for **Gringotts** ever since I left **Hogwarts**. As far as there can be friendship between wizards and goblins, I have goblin friends—or, at least, goblins I know well, and like.” Again, **Bill** hesitated. “**Harry**, what do you want from **Griphook**, and what have you promised him in return?”

“I can’t tell you that,” said **Harry**. “Sorry, Bill.”

The kitchen door opened behind them; **Fleur** was trying to bring through more empty goblets.

“Wait,” **Bill** told her, “Just a moment.”

She backed out and he closed the door again.

“Then I have to say this,” **Bill** went on. “If you have struck any kind of bargain with **Griphook**, and most particularly if that bargain involves treasure, you must be exceptionally careful. Goblin notions of **ownership**, **payment**, and **repayment** are not the same as human ones.”

**Harry** felt a slight squirm of discomfort, as though a small snake had stirred inside him.

“What do you mean?” he asked.

“We are talking about a different breed of being,” said **Bill**. “Dealings between wizards and goblins have been fraught for centuries—but you’ll know all that from **History of Magic**. There has been fault on both sides, I would never claim that wizards have been innocent. However, there is a belief among some goblins, and those at **Gringotts** are perhaps most prone to it, that wizards cannot be trusted in matters of gold and treasure, that they have no respect for goblin ownership.”

“I respect—” **Harry** began, but **Bill** shook his head.

“You don’t understand, **Harry**, nobody could understand unless they have lived with goblins. To a goblin, the rightful and true master of any object is the **maker**, not the purchaser. All goblin made objects are, in goblin eyes, rightfully theirs.”

“But it was bought—”

“—then they would consider it **rented** by the one who had paid the money. They have, however, great difficulty with the idea of goblin-made objects passing from wizard to wizard. You saw **Griphook’s** face when the tiara passed under his eyes. He disapproves. I believe he thinks, as do the fiercest of his kind, that it ought to have been returned to the goblins once the original purchaser died. They consider our habit of keeping goblin-made objects, passing them from wizard to wizard without further payment, little more than **theft**.”

**Harry** had an ominous feeling now; he wondered whether **Bill** guessed more than he was letting on.

“All I am saying,” said **Bill**, setting his hand on the door back into the sitting room, “is to be very careful what you promise goblins, **Harry**. It would be less dangerous to break into **Gringotts** than to renege on a promise to a goblin.”

“Right,” said **Harry** as **Bill** opened the door, “yeah. Thanks. I’ll bear that in mind.” As he followed **Bill** back to the others a wry thought came to him, born no doubt of the wine he had drunk. He seemed set on course to become just as reckless a **godfather** to **Teddy Lupin** as **Sirius Black** had been to him.

## 26. GRINGOTTS

Their plans were made, their preparations complete; in the smallest bedroom a single long, coarse **black hair** (plucked from the sweater **Hermione** had been wearing at **Malfoy Manor**) lay curled in a small glass phial on the mantelpiece.

“And you’ll be using her actual **wand**,” said **Harry**, nodding toward the walnut wand, “so I reckon you’ll be pretty convincing.”

**Hermione** looked frightened that the wand might sting or bit her as she picked it up.

“I hate that thing,” she said in a low voice. “I really hate it. It feels all wrong, it doesn’t work properly for me… It’s like a bit of her.”

**Harry** could not help but remember how **Hermione** has dismissed his loathing of the blackthorn wand, insisting that he was imagining things when it did not work as well as his own, telling him to simply practice. He chose not to repeat her own advice back to her, however, the eve of their attempted assault on **Gringotts** felt like the wrong moment to antagonize her.

“It’ll probably help you get in character, though,” said **Ron**. “think what that wand’s done!”

“But that’s my point!” said **Hermione**. “This is the wand that tortured **Neville’s** mum and dad, and who knows how many other people? This is the wand that killed **Sirius**!”

**Harry** had not thought of that: He looked down at the wand and was visited by a brutal urge to snap it, to slice it in half with **Gryffindor’s sword**, which was propped against the wall beside him.

“I miss my wand,” **Hermione** said miserably. “I wish **Mr. Ollivander** could have made me another one too.”

**Mr. Ollivander** had sent **Luna** a new wand that morning. She was out on the back lawn at that moment, testing its capabilities in the late afternoon sun. **Dean**, who had lost his wand to the Snatchers, was watching rather gloomily.

**Harry** looked down at the **hawthorn wand** that had once belonged to **Draco Malfoy**. He had been surprised, but pleased to discover that it worked for him at least as well as **Hermione’s** had done. Remembering what **Ollivander** had told them of the secret workings of wands, **Harry** thought he knew what **Hermione’s problem** was: She had not won the walnut wand’s allegiance by taking it personally from **Bellatrix**.

The door of the bedroom opened and **Griphook** entered. **Harry** reached instinctively for the hilt of the sword and drew it close to him, but regretted his action at once. He could tell that the goblin had noticed. Seeking to gloss over the sticky moment, he said, “We’ve just been checking the last-minute stuff, **Griphook**. We’ve told **Bill** and **Fleur** we’re leaving tomorrow, and we’ve told them not to get up to see us off.”

They had been firm on this point, because **Hermione** would need to transform in **Bellatrix** before they left, and the less that **Bill** and **Fleur** knew or suspected about what they were about to do, the better. They had also explained that they would not be returning. As they had lost **Perkins’s old tent** on the night that the Snatchers caught them, **Bill** had lent them another one. It was now packed inside the **beaded bag**, which, **Harry** was impressed to learn, **Hermione** had protected from the Snatchers by the simple expedient of stuffing it down her sock.

Though he would miss **Bill**, **Fleur**, **Luna**, and **Dean**, not to mention the home comforts they had enjoyed over the last few weeks, **Harry** was looking forward to escaping the confinement of **Shell Cottage**. He was tired of trying to make sure that they were not overheard, tired of being shut in the tiny, dark bedroom. Most of all, he longed to be rid of **Griphook**. However, precisely how and when they were to part from the goblin without handing over **Gryffindor’s sword** remained a question to which **Harry** had no answer. It had been impossible to decide how they were going to do it, because the goblin rarely left **Harry**, **Ron**, and **Hermione** alone together for more than five minutes at a time. “He could give my mother lessons,” growled **Ron**, as the goblin’s long fingers kept appearing around the edges of doors. With **Bill’s warning** in mind, **Harry** could not help suspecting that **Griphook** was on the watch for possible skullduggery. **Hermione** disapproved so heartily of the planned double-cross that **Harry** had given up attempting to pick her brains on how best to do it. **Ron**, on the rare occasions that they had been able to snatch a few **Griphook**-free moments, had come up with nothing better than “We’ll just have to wing it, mate.”

**Harry** slept badly that night. Lying awake

## Early Morning Departure

It was a relief when **six o’clock** arrived and they could slip out of their **sleeping bags**, dress in the **semidarkness**, then creep out into the garden, where they were to meet **Hermione** and **Griphook**. The **dawn** was chilly, but there was little wind now that it was **May**. Harry looked up at the stars still glimmering palely in the dark sky and listened to the **sea washing backward and forward against the cliff**: He was going to miss the sound.

Small green shoots were forcing their way up through the red earth of **Dobby’s grave** now; in a year’s time the mound would be covered in flowers. The white stone that bore the elf’s name had already acquired a **weathered look**. Harry ached with sadness to think of leaving him behind, wondering how the elf had known where to come to rescue them. His fingers moved absently to the little pouch around his neck, through which he could feel the **jagged mirror fragment** in which he believed he had seen **Dumbledore’s eye**. Then the sound of a door opening made him look around.

## Disguise and Preparation

Bellatrix Lestrange was striding across the lawn toward them, accompanied by **Griphook**. As she walked, she was tucking the small, beaded bag into the inside pocket of another set of the old robes they had taken from **Grimmauld Place**. Although Harry knew perfectly well it was really **Hermione**, he could not suppress a shiver of loathing. She was taller than he was, with long black hair rippling down her back and heavily lidded, disdainful eyes set on him. Then she spoke, and Harry heard **Hermione** through Bellatrix’s low voice.

- “She tasted disgusting, worse than **Gurdyroots**! Okay, Ron, come here so I can do you...”
- “Right, but remember, I don’t like the **beard** too long—”
- “Oh, for heaven’s sake, this isn’t about looking handsome—”
- “It’s not that, it gets in the way! But I liked my **nose** a bit shorter, try and do it the way you did last time.”

Hermione sighed and set to work, muttering as she transformed various aspects of **Ron’s appearance**. He was to be given a completely **fake identity**, trusting the **malevolent aura** cast by Bellatrix to protect him. Meanwhile, Harry and Griphook were to be concealed under the **Invisibility Cloak**.

- Ron’s hair became **long and wavy**
- He had a **thick brown beard and mustache**
- No freckles
- A **short, broad nose** and heavy eyebrows

“Well, he’s not my type, but he’ll do,” said Harry.

## Leaving Shell Cottage

All three glanced back at **Shell Cottage**, lying dark and silent under the fading stars. They began to walk toward the point just beyond the boundary wall, where the **Fidelius Charm** stopped working, and they would be able to **Disapparate**. Once past the gate, Griphook said:

- “I should climb up now, Harry Potter, I think?”

Harry bent down and the **goblin clambered onto his back**, his hands linked in front of Harry’s throat. Hermione pulled the **Invisibility Cloak** from the beaded bag and threw it over them both.

“Perfect,” she said, bending down to check Harry’s feet. “I can’t see a thing. Let’s go.”

Harry concentrated on the **Leaky Cauldron**, the inn that was the entrance to **Diagon Alley**. Seconds later, Harry’s feet found pavement and he opened his eyes on **Charing Cross Road**. Muggles bustled past, ignorant of the little inn’s existence.

## Entering the Leaky Cauldron

The bar of the **Leaky Cauldron** was nearly deserted. **Tom**, the stooped and toothless landlord, was polishing glasses behind the bar counter. A couple of warlocks in the far corner glanced at Hermione and drew back into the shadows.

- “Madam Lestrange,” murmured Tom, inclining his head subserviently.

“Good morning,” said Hermione. Harry saw Tom look surprised as they passed out into the tiny backyard.

“Too polite,” Harry whispered to Hermione. “You need to treat people like they’re scum!”

“Okay, okay!” she responded.

Hermione drew out Bellatrix’s **wand** and rapped a brick on the wall before them. The bricks began to whirl and spin, forming a growing hole which became an archway onto the narrow cobbled street of **Diagon Alley**.

## Diagon Alley Changes and Encounter

It was quiet, barely time for shops to open, and few shoppers were about. The crooked, cobbled street was much altered from Harry’s previous visits. Many shops were boarded up; several new establishments dedicated to the **Dark Arts** had appeared.

Harry’s own face glared down at him from posters plastered on windows, captioned **UNDESIRABLE NUMBER ONE**.

- Ragged people sat huddled in doorways, moaning and pleading for gold, insisting they were wizards.
- One man had a **bloody bandage over his eye**.

As they set off, the beggars glimpsed Hermione and fled, drawing hoods over their faces. Suddenly, the man with the bloody bandage staggered toward Hermione and shouted:

- “My children, where are my children? What has he done with them? You know, you know!”

Hermione stammered in response. The man lunged at her, but with a bang and a burst of red light, he was thrown backward unconscious. **Ron** stood there, wand outstretched, shocked. Faces appeared at windows, and passersby quickly left the scene.

## Confrontation with Travers

Their entrance into Diagon Alley was conspicuous. Before they could move or consult, they heard a cry:

- “Why, Madam Lestrange!”

Harry spun around as Griphook tightened his hold. A tall, thin wizard with bushy gray hair and a long, sharp nose approached.

- “It’s Travers,” hissed Griphook.

Hermione stood tall and said contemptuously:

- “And what do you want?”

Travers stopped, affronted.

- “I merely sought to greet you,” he said coolly. “But if my presence is not welcome…”

Harry recognized Travers as one of the **Death Eaters** summoned to **Xenophilius’s house**.

Hermione quickly covered up:

- “How are you?”

Travers expressed surprise to see Bellatrix out:

- “I heard the Inhabitants of Malfoy Manor were confined to the house after the… ah… escape.”

Hermione imitated Bellatrix’s voice:

- “The Dark Lord forgives those who have served him most faithfully. Perhaps your credit is not as good as mine, Travers.”

Though offended, Travers seemed less suspicious. He glanced at the unconscious man Ron had stunned.

Travers shared an anecdote about wandless beggars and questioned Hermione about the wand she was using.

Hermione, coldly holding up Bellatrix’s wand, replied:

- “I don’t know what rumors you’ve heard, but you seem sadly misinformed.”

Travers turned attention to Ron.

- “Who is your friend? I do not recognize him.”

Hermione introduced Ron as:

- **Dragomir Despard**, a fictional foreigner from **Transylvania** sympathetic to the Dark Lord’s aims.

Travers shook Ron’s hand cautiously and asked why they were in Diagon Alley so early.

Hermione responded:

- “I need to visit Gringotts.”

Travers said:

- “Alas, I also. Gold, filthy gold! We cannot live without it, yet I deplore consorting with our long-fingered friends.”

Griphook tightened his grasp around Harry’s neck as Travers gestured Hermione forward toward **Gringotts**.

## At Gringotts Entrance

They arrived at the foot of the **marble steps** leading to the great **bronze doors** of Gringotts. The usual goblin guards had been replaced by two wizards clutching long thin golden rods.

- Travers commented theatrically on the **Probity Probes**, crude but effective detectors of concealed magic.

Travers approached and was scanned by the probes. Harry quickly used Draco’s wand to cast **Confundo** spells on the guards, confusing them.

Hermione’s hair rippled behind her as she climbed the steps. One guard raised his Probe.

- Hermione, in Bellatrix’s commanding voice, said: “But you’ve just done that!”

Travers looked around, eyebrows raised. The guard seemed confused and checked with his companion, who agreed they had just scanned them moments before.

## Gringotts Vault Entrance

Hermione swept forward, **Ron** by her side, **Harry** and **Griphook** trotting invisibly behind them. Harry glanced back as they crossed the threshold; the wizards were both scratching their heads.

Two **goblins** stood before the inner doors, made of **silver** and inscribed with a poem warning of dire retribution to thieves. Harry remembered standing on this spot on his **eleventh birthday**, with **Hagrid** beside him saying, "Like I said, yeh’d be mad ter try an’ rob it." Gringotts had seemed a place of wonder that day, but now they were here to steal. Within seconds they were in the vast **marble hall** of the bank.

The long counter was manned by goblins on high stools serving the first customers of the day. Hermione, Ron, and **Travers** headed toward an old goblin examining a thick gold coin through an eyeglass. Hermione let Travers step ahead under the pretext of explaining features to Ron.

The goblin tossed aside the coin, muttered “**Leprechaun**,” then greeted Travers, who passed over a tiny **golden key**, which was examined and returned.

## Interaction at the Counter

Hermione stepped forward.

“Madam Lestrange!” said the goblin, evidently startled. “Dear me! How—how may I help you today?”

“I wish to enter my vault,” said Hermione.

The old goblin recoiled slightly. Harry noticed **Travers** hanging back and several goblins staring at Hermione.

“You have… identification?” asked the goblin.

“Identification? I—I have never been asked for identification before!” said Hermione.

“They know!” whispered Griphook to Harry. “They must have been warned there might be an imposter!”

“Your wand will do, madam,” said the goblin. His hand trembled. Harry realized the goblins knew that **Bellatrix’s wand** had been stolen.

“Act now, act now,” whispered Griphook. “The Imperius Curse!”

Harry raised the **hawthorn wand** beneath the cloak, pointed it at the old goblin, and whispered for the first time, “**Imperio!**”

## Using the Imperius Curse

A curious sensation shot down Harry’s arm—tingling warmth flowed from his mind to the wand and curse just cast. The goblin took **Bellatrix’s wand**, examined it closely, and said, “Ah, you have had a new wand made, Madam Lestrange!”

“What?” said Hermione, “No, no, that’s mine—”

“A new wand?” said Travers, approaching again; the goblins all around were watching. “But how could you have done that, which wandmaker did you use?”

Harry acted without thinking. Pointing his wand at Travers, he muttered, “**Imperio!**” once more.

“Oh yes, I see,” said Travers, looking at Bellatrix’s wand, “yes, very handsome. And is it working well? I always think wands require a little breaking in, don’t you?”

Hermione looked utterly bewildered but accepted the bizarre turn of events without comment.

The old goblin clapped, and a younger goblin approached.

“I shall need the **Clankers**,” he told the goblin, who dashed away and returned with a **leather bag** full of jangling metal, handing it to his senior.

“Good, good! If you will follow me, Madam Lestrange,” said the old goblin, hopping off his stool and vanishing from sight. “I shall take you to your vault.”

## Vault Escort and Suspicion

He jogged toward them with the leather bag jingling. Travers stood still with his mouth open; Ron looked confused at this odd behavior.

“Wait—Bogrod!” another goblin came scurrying.

“We have instructions,” he said politely to Hermione. “Forgive me, Madam, but there have been special orders regarding the vault of Lestrange.”

He whispered urgently in Bogrod’s ear, but the Imperiused goblin shook him off.

“I am aware of the instructions, Madam Lestrange wishes to visit her vault… Very old family… old clients… This way, please…”

Still clanking, he hurried toward one of many doors leading off the hall. Harry noticed Travers rooted with a vacant look and decided to bring him along, controlling him with the Imperius Curse.

They passed into a rough stone passageway lit by flaming torches.

## Invisibility Cloak Removed and Imperiused Goblins

“We’re in trouble; they suspect,” said Harry as the door slammed behind them and he pulled off the **Invisibility Cloak**. Griphook jumped down from Harry’s shoulders. Neither Travers nor Bogrod showed surprise at Harry’s sudden appearance.

“They’re **Imperiused**,” he explained to Hermione and Ron.

“I don’t think I did it strongly enough, I don’t know…” Harry reflected.

Another memory flashed: Bellatrix’s warning, “You need to mean them, Potter!”

## Decision to Proceed

“What do we do?” asked Ron. “Shall we get out now, while we can?”

“If we can,” said Hermione, looking back toward the main hall.

“We’ve got this far, I say we go on,” said Harry.

“Good!” said Griphook. “So, we need Bogrod to control the cart; I no longer

## Escape from the Vault

“**Make him press his hand to the door!**” Griphook urged **Harry**, who turned his **wand** again upon **Bogrod**. The old goblin obeyed, pressing his palm to the wood, and the door of the vault melted away to reveal a **cavelike opening** crammed from floor to ceiling with:

- **Golden coins** and goblets  
- **Silver armor**  
- Skins of strange creatures—some with long spines, others with drooping wings  
- **Potions in jeweled flasks**  
- A skull still wearing a crown  

“**Search, fast!**” said Harry as they all hurried inside the vault. He had described **Hufflepuff’s cup** to **Ron** and **Hermione**, but if it was

## Escape on the Dragon

After five minutes or so, **Harry** lost some of his immediate dread that the **dragon** was going to throw them off. The dragon seemed intent on getting as far away from its underground prison as possible. However, the question of **how and when they were to dismount** remained frightening. Harry had no idea how long dragons could fly without landing or how this particular dragon, which could barely see, would locate a **good place to put down**.

Harry glanced around constantly, imagining that he could feel his seat prickling. He wondered:

- How long before **Voldemort** knew they had broken into the **Lestranges’ vault**?
- How soon would the **goblins of Gringotts** notify **Bellatrix**?
- How quickly would they realize what had been taken?

When the golden cup was discovered missing, Voldemort would know that they were hunting **Horcruxes**.

## Flight Over the Countryside

The dragon seemed to crave cooler and fresher air. It climbed steadily until they were flying through wisps of chilly cloud. Harry could no longer make out the little colored dots of cars below.

They flew over countryside:

- Parcels of green and brown land
- Roads and rivers winding like matte and glossy ribbons

Ron yelled, “What do you reckon it’s looking for?” as they flew farther north.

Harry bellowed back, “No idea.” His hands were numb with cold, but he dared not shift his grip. He wondered what they would do if the dragon headed for open sea; he was cold, numb, hungry, and thirsty. Surely, the **dragon** would need sustenance before long, but what if it realized it had three **highly edible humans** on its back?

## Descent and Escape into the Lake

The sun slipped lower, and the sky turned indigo. Still, the dragon flew with its enormous shadow sliding like a giant dark cloud below. Harry’s body ached from holding on.

After a long silence, Ron shouted, “Are we losing height?”

Harry saw deep green mountains and lakes, coppery in the sunset. The dragon spiraled down toward one of the smaller lakes.

Harry called, “I say we jump when it gets low enough! Straight into the water before it realizes we’re here!”

They agreed, and Harry saw the dragon’s wide yellow underbelly ripple in the water. He slithered over the side and plummeted feet-first toward the lake's surface, hitting the freezing, reed-filled water hard.

He kicked up to the surface to see enormous ripples where **Ron** and **Hermione** also fell in. The dragon did not notice; it was already 50 feet away, scooping up water.

Ron and Hermione surfaced coughing and gasping. The dragon flew off and landed on a distant bank.

## Recovery on the Shore

Harry, Ron, and Hermione swam or fought through reeds and mud to the opposite shore, exhausted and sodden.

Hermione collapsed, coughing and shuddering. Harry, despite wanting to rest, stood and cast protective spells around them.

Once finished, he joined the others and saw their injuries for the first time since the vault escape: angry red burns and singed clothing. They dabbed **essence of dittany** on their wounds.

Hermione handed Harry a bottle of dittany, then pulled out three bottles of pumpkin juice and dry robes from **Shell Cottage**. They changed and drank the juice.

Ron reflected, “Well, on the upside, we got the **Horcrux**. On the downside—”

“No sword,” Harry said through gritted teeth, dripping dittany on a burn.

“No sword,” Ron repeated angrily. “That double-crossing little scab…”

Harry pulled the **Horcrux** from his wet jacket pocket and set it on the grass, glinting in the sun.

“At least we can’t wear it this time; that’d look weird hanging around our necks,” Ron joked.

Hermione looked to the far bank where the dragon still drank.

## Thoughts on the Dragon and Their Situation

Hermione asked, “What’ll happen to it? Will it be alright?”

Ron said, “You sound like **Hagrid**. It’s a dragon; it can look after itself. It’s us we need to worry about.”

Hermione questioned, “What do you mean?”

Ron admitted, “I don’t know how to break this to you, but I think they might have noticed we broke into Gringotts.”

All three laughed, though their laughter was tinged with exhaustion and pain. Harry’s ribs ached, he was lightheaded with hunger, but he lay back on the grass beneath the reddening sky and laughed until his throat was raw.

Hermione eventually regained seriousness, “He’ll know, won’t he? You-Know-Who will know we know about his Horcruxes!”

Ron hoped, “Maybe they’ll be too scared to tell him! Maybe they’ll cover up—”

## Voldemort’s Fury

Suddenly, Harry experienced a sharp pain. He was standing in a dimly lit room where a semicircle of **wizards** faced him. At his feet knelt a small, quaking goblin.

Voldemort's voice was cold and furious: “What did you say to me? Say it again!”

The trembling goblin claimed, “We tried to stop them. Impostors broke into the Lestranges’ vault.”

“Impostors? Who?” Voldemort demanded.

“It was the Potter boy and two accomplices.”

“And they took?” Voldemort's voice rose, “Tell me! What did they take?”

“A small golden cup, my Lord…”

## Voldemort’s Rage and Realization

The scream of rage left him as if it were a stranger’s. He was crazed and frenzied; it could not be true that anyone knew his secret.

The **Elder Wand** slashed through the air, green light erupted, and the goblin was killed. The watching wizards scattered, and **Bellatrix** and **Lucius Malfoy** fled. Those left behind were slain for bringing news of the stolen golden cup.

Alone, Voldemort paced as visions of his treasures and Horcrux safeguards passed before him:

- The diary was destroyed
- The cup was stolen

He feared the boy might have discovered his secret. Could he know about other Horcruxes? Was **Dumbledore** involved?

## Voldemort’s Reflection on Horcrux Safety

He reasoned:

- If the boy had destroyed any Horcrux, he would have felt it.
- He did not feel it when the diary was destroyed, but blamed his lack of a body.
- The other Horcruxes **must be intact**.

He considered:

- The **Gaunt shack** where the ring was hidden, likely the least secure place.
- The idea of the locket being stolen was absurd.
- The Horcrux hidden at **Hogwarts** was safe and known only to him.
- **Nagini**, the snake, must remain close and protected.

## Plans to Safeguard Horcruxes

Determined to be sure, Voldemort planned to:

- Return to each hiding place
- Redouble protection around his Horcruxes
- Undertake this quest alone, like for the Elder Wand

He decided to visit the **Gaunt shack** first, taking **Nagini** with him. No longer would he part from the snake.

He strode from the room, out into the dark garden where the fountain played, calling the snake in **Parseltongue**. The snake slithered out to join him like a long shadow.

## Return to Reality

Harry’s eyes flew open, pulling him back to the present. He was lying on the bank of the lake in the setting sun. Ron and Hermione looked down at him, worried.

Harry struggled up, shivering and surprised to feel wet to his skin. The cup lay innocently in the grass before him, and the lake was deep blue shot with gold in the falling sun.

## 28. THE MISSING MIRROR

“He knows.” His own voice sounded strange and low after **Voldemort’s** high screams. “He knows and he’s going to check where the others are, and the last one,” he was already on his feet, “is at **Hogwarts**. I knew it. I knew it.”

“What?”

**Ron** was gaping at him; **Hermione** sat up, looking worried.

“But what did you see? How do you know?”

“I saw him find out about the **cup**, I—I was in his head, he’s”—Harry remembered the killings—“he’s seriously angry, and scared too, he can’t understand how we knew, and now he’s going to check the others are safe, the **ring** first. He thinks

## Aberforth's Advice and the Plan to Escape

“Right then,” said **Aberforth** when they had eaten their fill and **Harry** and **Ron** sat slumped dozily in their chairs. 

- They needed to think of the best way to get **Harry** and **Ron** out of there.
- It couldn’t be done by night because the **Caterwauling Charm** would be set off if anyone moved outdoors during darkness.
- Aberforth said he couldn’t pass off a **stag as a goat** a second time.
- They should wait for daybreak when curfew lifts, put on the **Invisibility Cloak**, and set out on foot.
- They should get out of **Hogsmeade**, up into the mountains, and **Disapparate** there.
- Aberforth mentioned they might see **Hagrid**, who had been hiding in a cave with **Grawp**.

Harry insisted, “We’re not leaving. We need to get into **Hogwarts**.”

Aberforth disagreed: “You’ve got to get as far from here as you can.”

Harry tried to explain that **Dumbledore**—his brother—wanted them to get into the castle.

Aberforth's glasses momentarily became opaque, reminding Harry of **Aragog’s blind eyes**.

## Aberforth on Albus Dumbledore

“My brother Albus wanted a lot of things,” said Aberforth, “and people often got hurt during his grand plans.” 

- Aberforth urged Harry to get away from the school and out of the country.
- He told Harry to forget his brother and his schemes.
- Aberforth said Albus was gone where none of this could hurt him, and Harry owed him nothing.

Harry felt he had a **job left by Dumbledore**, but Aberforth was skeptical.

- He asked if it was a pleasant or easy job.
- Aberforth emphasized the **Order of the Phoenix** was finished since **You-Know-Who** had won.
- He told Harry to **save himself** and go into hiding along with **Ron** and **Hermione**, who would be in danger because everyone knew they were working with Harry.

Harry insisted he couldn't leave because of the job Dumbledore left him.

Aberforth suggested **"Give it to someone else!"** but Harry refused.

Aberforth doubted Dumbledore had told Harry everything or been honest.

## Aberforth's Family Secrets: Ariana Dumbledore

Aberforth’s eyes traveled to a painting of a girl over the mantelpiece.

- Hermione timidly asked if it was **his sister, Ariana**.
- Aberforth replied tersely and accused Hermione of reading **Rita Skeeter**.
- Harry recalled **Elphias Doge** had mentioned her.

Aberforth criticized those who believed everything about Albus Dumbledore.

- He said many people Albus cared about ended worse off.
- Hermione asked if he meant **Ariana**.
- Aberforth then began telling the story of Ariana's tragic past.

### The Attack on Ariana

- At six years old, Ariana was attacked by three **Muggle boys** who saw her doing magic.
- They forced their way through the hedge; when she couldn’t perform a trick, they got violent.
- This left Ariana **never right again**; she couldn’t control her magic, which turned inward or exploded out uncontrollably.
- She was mostly **sweet, scared, and harmless**, but sometimes strange and dangerous.

### The Family’s Struggles

- Aberforth’s father attacked the boys and was imprisoned in **Azkaban**.
- To protect Ariana, they moved house and hid her condition, with their mother caring for her.
- Aberforth was Ariana’s favorite sibling; Albus ignored her for his studies and connections.
- Ariana helped Aberforth feed the goats when she was calm.

### The Tragedy of Ariana and Their Mother

- When Ariana was fourteen, she had a rage episode that accidentally killed their mother.
- Aberforth felt guilt and anger, thinking he could have calmed her if he’d been there.
- Albus returned from his trip for the funeral and took over family responsibilities.

### Grindelwald’s Influence

- Aberforth described **Grindelwald** as a dangerous influence on Albus.
- The pair focused on plans for a new **Wizarding order** while Ariana was neglected.
- Aberforth confronted them, warning that Ariana was not fit to be taken along.
- Grindelwald mocked and dismissed Aberforth.
- A duel broke out between Aberforth, Grindelwald, and Albus.
- The conflict triggered Ariana, who died during the chaos.
- Aberforth was deeply affected, feeling the loss and bitterness.

## Reflection on Albus Dumbledore's Burden

- Grindelwald fled, avoiding blame for Ariana’s death.
- Aberforth commented that Albus was then **free of the burden** of his sister and free to become the greatest wizard.
- Harry disagreed, stating that Albus was **never free**.
- Harry recalled how on the night of Dumbledore’s death, Albus drank a potion that drove him insane, screaming to protect others instead of himself.

---

**Key Characters:**
- **Aberforth Dumbledore** – Albus’s brother, wary and protective.
- **Albus Dumbledore** – Powerful wizard with complex past.
- **Ariana Dumbledore** – Their sister, traumatized and magical.
- **Grindelwald** – Dark wizard and former friend of Albus.
- **Harry Potter**, **Ron**, **Hermione** – Present during Aberforth’s account.

**Important Concepts:**
- **Caterwauling Charm:** Security charm triggering alerts at night.
- **Disapparate:** Magical teleportation.
- **Order of the Phoenix:** Group fighting against dark forces.
- **International Statute of Secrecy:** Wizarding world's code to hide magical activity from Muggles.
- **Cruciatus Curse:** Torture curse used in dueling.
- **Azkaban:** Magical prison.
- **Invisibility Cloak:** Magical item to remain unseen.

## Conversation Between Ron, Hermione, Harry, and Aberforth

Ron and Hermione were staring at **Harry**. He had never gone into details about what had happened on the island on the lake: The events that had taken place after he and **Dumbledore** had returned to **Hogwarts** had eclipsed it so thoroughly.

**Harry** remembered **Dumbledore** whispering and pleading, saying, “He thought he was back there with you and **Grindelwald**, I know he did.”

Harry explained, “He thought he was watching **Grindelwald** hurting you and **Ariana**… It was torture to him, if you’d seen him then, you wouldn’t say he was free.”

**Aberforth** seemed lost in contemplation of his own knotted and veined hands. After a long pause he said,  
“How can you be sure, **Potter**, that my brother wasn’t more interested in the **greater good** than in you? How can you be sure you aren’t dispensable, just like my little sister?”

A shard of ice seemed to pierce **Harry**’s heart.

Hermione stated firmly, “I don’t believe it. **Dumbledore** loved **Harry**.”

Aberforth shot back, “Why didn’t he tell him to hide, then? Why didn’t he say to him, ‘Take care of yourself, here’s how to survive’?”

Harry answered before Hermione could, “Because sometimes you’ve got to think about more than your own safety! Sometimes you’ve got to think about the **greater good**! This is **war**!”

Aberforth snapped, “You’re **seventeen**, boy!”

Harry replied, “I’m of age, and I’m going to keep fighting even if you’ve given up!”

Aberforth retorted, “Who says I’ve given up?”

Harry declared, “The **Order of the Phoenix** is finished. **You-Know-Who**’s won, it’s over, and anyone who’s pretending differently's kidding themselves.”

Aberforth admitted, “I don’t say I like it, but it’s the truth!”

Harry insisted, “No, it isn’t. Your brother knew how to finish **You-Know-Who** and he passed the knowledge on to me. I’m going to keep going until I succeed—or I die. Don’t think I don’t know how this might end. I’ve known it for years.”

He waited for **Aberforth** to jeer or argue, but he did not. He merely moved.

Harry said again, “We need to get into **Hogwarts**. If you can’t help us, we’ll wait till daybreak, leave you in peace, and try to find a way in ourselves. If you can help us—well, now would be a great time to mention it.”

Aberforth remained fixed in his chair, gazing at Harry with eyes extraordinarily like his brother’s. At last, he cleared his throat, got to his feet, walked around the little table, and approached the portrait of **Ariana**.

“You know what to do,” he said.

## Secret Passageway Revealed

**Ariana** smiled, turned, and walked away—not as people in portraits usually do along the sides of their frames—but along what seemed to be a long tunnel painted behind her. They watched her slight figure retreating until finally she was swallowed by darkness.

Ron asked, “Er—what—?”

Aberforth explained,  
“There’s only one way in now. You must know they’ve got all the old secret passageways covered at both ends, **Dementors** all around the boundary walls, regular patrols inside the school from what my sources tell me. The place has never been so heavily guarded. How you expect to do anything once you get inside it, with **Snape** in charge and the **Carrows** as his deputies… well, that’s your lookout, isn’t it? You say you’re prepared to die.”

Hermione frowned at **Ariana**’s picture and asked, “But what…?”

A tiny white dot reappeared at the end of the painted tunnel, and now **Ariana** was walking back toward them, growing bigger and bigger as she came. But there was somebody else with her now, someone taller who was limping excitedly. His hair was longer than **Harry** had ever seen. The two figures grew until their heads and shoulders filled the portrait.

Then the whole thing swung forward on the wall like a door, revealing the entrance to a real tunnel. Out of it, with overgrown hair, a cut face, and ripped robes, clambered the real **Neville Longbottom**, who gave a roar of delight, leapt down from the mantelpiece and yelled,

“I knew you’d come! I knew it, Harry!”

## Chapter 29: The Lost Diadem

Neville’s battered visage shone with happiness as he hugged Ron and Hermione too. The longer Harry looked at Neville, the worse he appeared: one eye swollen yellow and purple, gouge marks on his face, and his general unkemptness suggested he had been living rough. Nevertheless, he said again,

“I knew you’d come! Kept telling **Seamus** it was a matter of time!”

Harry asked, “Neville, what’s happened to you?”

Neville dismissed his injuries, “This? It’s nothing. **Seamus** is worse. You’ll see. Shall we get going then? Oh,” he turned to **Aberforth**, “Ab, there might be a couple more people on the way.”

Aberforth repeated ominously, “Couple more? What d’you mean, a couple more, **Longbottom**? There’s a curfew and a **Camwaulding Charm** on the whole village!”
