Neville explained, “I know, that’s why they’ll be **Apparating** directly into the bar. Just send them down the passage when they get here, will you? Thanks a lot.”

Neville helped Hermione climb onto the mantelpiece and into the tunnel; Ron followed, then Neville.

Harry addressed Aberforth,  
“I don’t know how to thank you. You’ve saved our lives twice.”

Aberforth gruffly replied,  
“Look after ’em then. I might not be able to save ’em a third time.”

Harry clambered up onto the mantelpiece and through the hole behind **Ariana**’s portrait. Inside was a smooth stone staircase. Brass lamps hung from the walls, and the earthy floor was worn smooth. As they walked, their shadows rippled fanlike across the wall.

Ron asked, “How long’s this been here? It isn’t on the **Marauder’s Map**, is it, Harry? I thought there were only seven passages in and out of school?”

Neville answered,  
“They sealed off all of those before the start of the year. There’s no chance of getting through any of them now, not with the curses over the entrances and **Death Eaters** and **Dementors** waiting at the exits.”

He walked backward, smiling,  
“Never mind that stuff… Is it true? Did you break into **Gringotts**? Did you escape on a dragon? It’s everywhere, everyone’s talking about it. **Terry Boot** got beaten up by **Carrow** for yelling about it in the Great Hall at dinner!”

Harry confirmed, “Yeah, it’s true.”

Neville laughed gleefully.  
“What did you do with the dragon?”

Ron said, “Released it into the wild.”

Hermione interjected, “I was all for keeping it as a pet—”

Ron added, “Don’t exaggerate, Ron—”

Neville asked, “But what have you been doing? People have been saying you’ve just been on the run, Harry, but I don’t think so. I think you’ve been up to something.”

Harry affirmed, “You’re right, but tell us about Hogwarts, Neville, we haven’t heard anything.”

Neville’s smile faded as he explained.  
“It’s been… Well, it’s not really like Hogwarts anymore. Do you know about the **Carrows**?”

Hermione asked, “Those two **Death Eaters** who teach here?”

Neville said,  
“They do more than teach. They’re in charge of all discipline. They like punishment, the Carrows.”

Ron compared, “Like **Umbridge**?”

Neville answered, “Nah, they make her look tame. The other teachers are supposed to refer us to the Carrows if we do anything wrong. They don’t, though, if they can avoid it. You can tell they all hate them as much as we do.”

Neville detailed,  
**Amycus**, the bloke, teaches what used to be **Defense Against the Dark Arts**, except now it’s just the **Dark Arts**. We’re supposed to practice the **Cruciatus Curse** on people who’ve earned detentions—

Harry

## Arrival at the Room of Requirement

**Neville** led the way through a hidden door behind Ariana's portrait. As **Harry** followed, Neville called out excitedly to unseen people.

The room erupted with cheers:

- "HARRY!"
- "It’s Potter, it’s POTTER!"
- "Ron!"
- "Hermione!"

Harry was engulfed by over twenty people, hugged and greeted warmly as if they had just won a **Quidditch final**.

Neville calmed the crowd, allowing Harry to take in their surroundings. The dorm was enormous, resembling a sumptuous treehouse or a gigantic ship’s cabin. 

### Description of the Room

- Multicolored hammocks hung from the ceiling and balcony  
- Dark wood-paneled and windowless walls covered in bright tapestry hangings  
- Emblems visible: **Gryffindor lion (gold on scarlet)**, **Hufflepuff badger (black on yellow)**, **Ravenclaw eagle (bronze on blue)**  
- **Slytherin's** silver and green colors were absent  
- Bulging bookcases, broomsticks propped against walls  
- Large wood-cased wireless in the corner  

## The Room’s Purpose and Expansion

Neville explained the **Room of Requirement** had expanded since he arrived.

- Initially smaller with one hammock and only Gryffindor hangings  
- Expanded as more members of **Dumbledore’s Army (D.A.)** arrived  
- It serves as a secure **hideout**, inaccessible to the **Carrows** while someone stays inside  

Seamus revealed:

- The room answers specific needs—requests must be exact  
- Neville had mastered commanding the room  
- Passage to **Hog’s Head** opened, allowing Aberforth to supply food, as the room does not provide it (due to exceptions in **Gamp’s Law of Elemental Transfiguration**)  

Lavender Brown mentioned the addition of a decent bathroom after the arrival of girls.

## Members Present in the Room

Harry recognized many familiar faces:

- Both Patil twins  
- Terry Boot  
- Ernie Macmillan  
- Anthony Goldstein  
- Michael Corner  
- Lavender Brown  

## Rumors and Confirmation

Ernie asked about rumors on **Potterwatch**, specifically about breaking into **Gringotts**.

- Neville confirmed the break-in and the existence of the dragon  
- The group applauded and cheered  

## Voldemort’s Warning

Suddenly, Harry felt agonizing pain in his **lightning scar** indicating **Voldemort’s fury** after losing a Horcrux.

- Harry struggled mentally but returned to present  
- Ron held him to prevent falling  

Neville offered help, but Harry was focused and insisted they must leave.

## The Plan and Secrecy

Seamus asked about the plan.

- Harry revealed a secret task entrusted to him, Ron, and Hermione by **Dumbledore**  
- They must act alone and cannot share details  
- The room's members wanted to help but Harry insisted they must proceed privately  

Neville argued that D.A. had been supporting Harry’s group.

Harry explained:

- **Dumbledore** wanted only the three of them to do this  
- He felt torn about trust and secrecy  

## Arrival of Reinforcements

The tunnel door opened, and **Luna** and **Dean** arrived, greeted with excitement.

- Luna was contacted by Neville to join if Harry returned, signaling a revolution to overthrow **Snape** and the **Carrows**  
- Others, like Ginny, Fred, George, Lee Jordan, and Cho Chang soon followed  

## Group’s Reaction and Harry’s Concerns

- Ginny's radiant smile struck Harry, but he was uneasy about the growing crowd  
- Fred joked about **Aberforth** wanting to rest due to the bar's busy atmosphere  
- Harry stressed urgency but struggled with the number of people and his burning scar  

## Discussion of the Missing Object

Harry asked the gathered members about a missing object related to **Ravenclaw**.

- He speculated it might help defeat **You-Know-Who**  
- Luna mentioned the **lost diadem of Ravenclaw**, which her father tried to duplicate  
- Michael Corner was skeptical since it was lost centuries ago  
- Cho explained that the diadem vanished with **Ravenclaw** herself, and no one had found any trace  

Ron asked for clarification on what a **diadem** was, signaling more information was needed.

## The Diadem of Ravenclaw

“It’s a kind of **crown**,” said **Terry Boot**. “**Ravenclaw’s diadem** was supposed to have **magical properties**, enhancing the **wisdom** of the wearer.”

“Yes, Daddy’s **Wrackspurt siphons**—”

But **Harry** cut across Luna.

“And none of you have ever seen anything that looks like it?”

They all shook their heads. Harry looked at **Ron**, **Hermione**, and saw his own **disappointment** mirrored back. An object lost this long, and apparently without trace, did not seem a good candidate for the **Horcrux** hidden in the castle. Before he could ask another question, **Cho** spoke again.

“If you’d like to see what the **diadem** looks like, I could take you to our **common room** and show you, Harry. **Ravenclaw** is wearing it in her statue.”

---

## Harry's Vision and Decision

Harry’s **scar** scorched again. For a moment, the **Room of Requirement** swam before him; he saw dark earth soaring beneath him and felt the great snake wrapped around his shoulders. **Voldemort** was flying again—but where, he did not know. Either to the underground lake or to the castle. There was hardly any time left.

“He’s on the move,” Harry said quietly to Ron and Hermione. He glanced at Cho and back. “Listen, I know it’s not much of a lead, but I’m going to look at this statue, at least find out what the diadem looks like. Wait for me here and keep, you know—the other one—safe.”

**Cho** got to her feet, but **Ginny** said fiercely, “No, **Luna** will take Harry, won’t you, Luna?”

“Oooh, yes, I’d like to,” said Luna happily, as Cho sat down again, disappointed.

---

## Exiting the Room of Requirement

“How do we get out?” Harry asked **Neville**.

“Over here.”

Neville led Harry and Luna to a corner, where a small cupboard opened onto a steep staircase.

“It comes out somewhere different every day, so they’ve never been able to find it,” he said. “Only trouble is, we never know where we’ll end up. Be careful, Harry, they’re always patrolling corridors at night.”

“No problem,” said Harry. “See you in a bit.”

Harry and Luna hurried up the long staircase, lit by torches, turning corners unpredictably. At last they reached a solid wall.

“Get under here,” Harry told Luna, pulling out the **Invisibility Cloak** and throwing it over both of them. He pressed the wall, which melted away, and they slipped outside. The wall resealed itself instantly.

They stood in a dark corridor. Harry pulled Luna back into the shadows and took out the **Marauder’s Map**. Holding it close, he searched and found their dots.

“We’re on the fifth floor,” he whispered, watching **Filch** move away down the corridor ahead. “Come on, this way.”

---

## Journey Through the Castle

They crept off. Harry had prowled the castle at night many times before, but never had his heart hammered so fast. So much depended on his safe passage.

They passed through moonlight, past suits of armor whose helmets creaked softly, around corners beyond which who knew what lurked. They checked the Marauder’s Map frequently and twice paused for ghosts to pass.

His worst fear was **Peeves**, the poltergeist, and Harry strained to hear any telltale signs.

“The way, Harry,” Luna whispered, pulling his sleeve toward a spiral staircase.

They climbed dizzying circles and reached a door with no handle or keyhole, only a plain expanse of aged wood and a **bronze knocker** shaped like an eagle.

---

## The Ravenclaw Common Room Door

Luna knocked once. The sound was like a cannon blast in the silence. The eagle’s beak opened, but instead of a bird call, a soft musical voice said:

**“Which came first, the phoenix or the flame?”**

“What? Isn’t there a password?” Harry asked.

“Oh no, you answer a question,” Luna said.

“What if you get it wrong?”

“Well, you wait for someone who gets it right,” Luna explained. “That way you learn.”

“Yeah… but we can’t afford to wait for anyone else, Luna.”

Luna nodded seriously. “Well then, I think the answer is that a **circle has no beginning**.”

“Well reasoned,” said the voice, and the door swung open.

---

## Inside the Ravenclaw Common Room

The deserted **Ravenclaw common room** was wide and circular, airier than any Harry had seen at Hogwarts. 

- Graceful **arched windows** punctuated the walls, hung with **blue-and-bronze silks**.
- By day, Ravenclaws would have a spectacular view of the surrounding **mountains**.
- The **domed ceiling** was painted with stars, echoed in the midnight-blue **carpet**.
- There were **tables, chairs, bookcases**, and a niche with a tall white marble statue.

Harry recognized **Rowena Ravenclaw** from a bust he had seen at Luna’s house. The statue stood by a door likely leading to dormitories above.

He approached the marble woman, who seemed to look back at him with a quizzical half-smile—beautiful yet intimidating. On her head was a delicate marble **circlet** resembling a tiara Fleur had worn at her wedding.

Harry stepped out from under the Cloak and climbed onto Ravenclaw’s plinth to read the etched words.

> **“Wit beyond measure is man’s greatest treasure.”**

“Which makes you pretty skint, witless,” a cackling voice said.

Harry whirled around, slipped off the plinth, and landed on the floor.

---

## Encounter with Alecto Carrow

The sloping-shouldered figure of **Alecto Carrow** stood before him. Harry raised his wand, but she pressed a stubby forefinger to the **skull and snake** branded on her forearm.

---

## 30. THE SACKING OF SEVERUS SNAPE

When her finger touched the Mark, Harry’s **scar burned savagely** and his vision vanished. He was on a rock beneath a cliff with the sea washing around him; in his heart was a triumph: **They have the boy**.

A loud bang brought him back. Disoriented, he raised his wand, but the witch was already falling forward and hit the ground hard, the glass in bookcases tinkling.

“I’ve never **Stunned** anyone except in our D.A. lessons,” said Luna mildly interested. “That was noisier than I thought.”

Sure enough, the ceiling began to tremble. Loud footsteps grew closer from the dormitory door. Luna’s spell had woken Ravenclaws sleeping above.

---

## Hiding Under the Cloak

“Luna, where are you? I need to get under the Cloak!”

Luna’s feet appeared; Harry hurried to her side and she let the Cloak fall over them as the door opened.

A stream of Ravenclaws in nightclothes flooded the room. There were gasps at the sight of Alecto lying unconscious.

Slowly, they gathered cautiously around her like a wild beast, afraid she might attack any moment.

One brave first-year poked her with his toe. “I think she might be dead!” he shouted.

“Oh look,” whispered Luna happily. “They’re pleased!”

“Yeah… great…”

---

## Harry’s Scar and Voldemort’s Mind

Harry closed his eyes. His scar throbbed as he sank into **Voldemort’s mind**.

He saw Voldemort moving into the first cave, having secured the **locket**, a short task.

---

## Confrontation at the Common Room Door

A rap sounded on the door. Every Ravenclaw froze.

The musical voice came again:

**“Where do Vanished objects go?”**

“I dunno, do I? Shut it!” snarled **Amycus Carrow**.

“Alecto? Alecto? Open the door!” he yelled.

Ravenclaws whispered, terrified.

Loud bangs followed as if someone fired a gun into the door.

“ALECTO! If he comes and we haven’t got Potter—do you want to go the same way as the Malfoys? ANSWER ME!” Amycus bellowed, shaking the door.

Ravenclaws backed away; some scampered upstairs to beds.

Harry considered blasting the door but instead, a familiar voice rang beyond it.

---

## Professor McGonagall’s Arrival

“May I ask what you are doing, Professor Carrow?”

“Trying—to get—through this damned—door!” Amycus shouted.

“Go and get Flitwick! Get him to open it, now!”

“But isn’t your sister in there?” asked **Professor McGonagall**. “Didn’t Professor Flitwick let her in earlier? Perhaps she could open the door.”

“She ain’t answering, you old besom! You open it! Garn! Do it, now!”

“Certainly, if you wish,” said McGonagall coldly.

She tapped the knocker; the voice asked again:

**“Where do Vanished objects go?”**

“Into non-being, which is to say, everything,” replied McGonagall.

“Nicely phrased,” said the knocker, and the door swung open.

---

## Amycus Carrow’s Fury

Few Ravenclaws remained and sprinted for the stairs as Amycus entered, wand brandished.

He had a pallid, doughy face and tiny eyes, which fell immediately on Alecto sprawled motionless.

He screamed:

“What’ve they done, the little whelps? I’ll **Cruciate** them till they tell me who did it—and what’s the **Dark Lord** going to say?”

He smacked his forehead, “We haven’t got him, and they’ve gone and killed her!”

“She’s only **Stunned**,” said McGonagall, examining Alecto. “She’ll be perfectly all right.”

“No she bludgering well won’t! Not after the Dark Lord gets hold of her! She sent for him; I felt my Mark burn, and he thinks we’ve got Potter!”

---

## Discussion with Professor McGonagall

“‘Got Potter’?” McGonagall asked sharply. “What do you mean?”

“He told us Potter might try to get inside **Ravenclaw Tower**, and to send for him if we caught Potter!”

“Why would Potter try to get inside Ravenclaw Tower? Potter belongs in my House!” McGonagall said, with pride and affection evident in her voice.

“He was told he might come in here!” said Amycus.

Professor McGonagall scanned the room, her eyes passing over where Harry and Luna stood.

---

## Amycus’s Plan to Blame the Students

“We can push it off on the kids,” said Amycus craftily.

“We’ll say **Alecto** was ambushed by the kids up in the dormitories and forced to press her **Mark**, which is why he got a false alarm. The Dark Lord can punish them. A couple of kids more or less, what’s the difference?”

## Encounter with Amycus Carrow

“Only the difference between **truth and lie, courage and cowardice**,” said **Professor McGonagall**, who had turned pale, “a difference, in short, which you and your sister seem unable to appreciate. But let me make one thing very clear. You are not going to pass off your many ineptitudes on the students of **Hogwarts**. I shall not permit it.”

“Excuse me?”

Amycus moved forward until he was offensively close to Professor McGonagall, his face within inches of hers. She refused to back away, but looked down at him as if he were something disgusting she had found stuck to the lavatory seat.

“It’s not a case of what you’ll permit, Minerva McGonagall. Your time’s over. It’s us what’s in charge here now, and you’ll back me up or you’ll pay the price.”

And he spat in her face.

## Harry’s Intervention

Harry pulled the **Cloak** off himself, raised his wand, and said, “You shouldn’t have done that.”

As Amycus spun around, Harry shouted, “**Crucio!**”

The Death Eater was lifted off his feet. He writhed through the air like a drowning man, thrashing and howling in pain, and then, with a crunch and a shattering of glass, he smashed into the front of a bookcase and crumpled, insensible, to the floor.

“I see what **Bellatrix** meant,” said Harry, the blood thundering through his brain, “you need to really mean it.”

## McGonagall and Harry’s Exchange

“Potter!” whispered Professor McGonagall, clutching her heart. “Potter—you’re here! What—? How—?” She struggled to pull herself together. “Potter, that was foolish!”

“He spat at you,” said Harry.

“Potter, I—that was very—very gallant of you—but don’t you realize—?”

“Yeah, I do,” Harry assured her. Somehow her panic steadied him. “Professor McGonagall, **Voldemort’s on the way**.”

“Oh, are we allowed to say the name now?” asked **Luna** with an air of interest, pulling off the Invisibility Cloak. The appearance of a second outlaw seemed to overwhelm Professor McGonagall, who staggered backward and fell into a nearby chair, clutching at the neck of her old tartan dressing gown.

“I don’t think it makes any difference what we call him,” Harry told Luna. “He already knows where I am.”

## Voldemort’s Advance and Urgency

In a distant part of Harry’s brain, that part connected to the angry, burning **scar**, he could see **Voldemort** sailing fast over the dark lake in the ghostly green boat… He had nearly reached the island where the stone basin stood…

“You must flee,” whispered Professor McGonagall, “Now, Potter, as quickly as you can!”

“I can’t,” said Harry, “There’s something I need to do. Professor, do you know where the **diadem of Ravenclaw** is?”

“The d-diadem of Ravenclaw? Of course not—hasn’t it been lost for centuries?” She sat up a little straighter. “Potter, it was madness, utter madness, for you to enter this castle—”

“I had to,” said Harry. “Professor, there’s something hidden here that I’m supposed to find, and it could be the diadem—if I could just speak to **Professor Flitwick**—”

## Capturing the Carrows

There was a sound of movement, of clinking glass. Amycus was coming round. Before Harry or Luna could act, Professor McGonagall rose to her feet, pointed her wand at the groggy Death Eater, and said, “**Imperio**.”

Amycus got up, walked over to his sister, picked up her wand, then shuffled obediently to Professor McGonagall and handed it over along with his own. Then he lay down on the floor beside **Alecto**. Professor McGonagall waved her wand again, and a length of shimmering silver rope appeared out of thin air and snaked around the **Carrows**, binding them tightly together.

“Potter,” said Professor McGonagall, turning to face him again with superb indifference to the Carrows’ predicament. “If **He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named** does indeed know that you are here—”

As she said it, a wrath that was like physical pain blazed through Harry, setting his scar on fire, and for a second he looked down upon a basin whose potion had turned clear, and saw that no golden locket lay safe beneath the surface—

“Potter, are you all right?” said a voice, and Harry came back. He was clutching Luna’s shoulder to steady himself.

## Harry’s Mission and McGonagall’s Support

“Time’s running out, Voldemort’s getting nearer. Professor, I’m acting on **Dumbledore’s orders**, I must find what he wanted me to find! But we’ve got to get the students out while I’m searching the castle—It’s me Voldemort wants, but he won’t care about killing a few more or less, not now—”

Not now he knows I’m attacking **Horcruxes**, Harry finished the sentence in his head.

“You’re acting on Dumbledore’s orders?” she repeated with a look of dawning wonder. Then she drew herself up to her fullest height.

“We shall secure the school against **He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named** while you search for this—this object.”

“Is that possible?”

“I think so,” said Professor McGonagall dryly, “we teachers are rather good at magic, you know. I am sure we will be able to hold him off for a while if we all put our best efforts into it. Of course, something will have to be done about **Professor Snape**—”

“Let me—”

“—and if Hogwarts is about to enter a state of siege, with the Dark Lord at the gates, it would indeed be advisable to take as many innocent people out of the way as possible. With the **Floo Network** under observation, and **Apparition** impossible within the grounds—”

“There’s a way,” said Harry quickly, and he explained about the passageway leading into the **Hog’s Head**.

“Potter, we’re talking about hundreds of students—”

“I know, Professor, but if Voldemort and the **Death Eaters** are concentrating on the school boundaries they won’t be interested in anyone who’s **Disapparating** out of Hog’s Head.”

“There’s something in that,” she agreed. She pointed her wand at the Carrows, and a silver net fell upon their bound bodies, tied itself around them, and hoisted them into the air, where they dangled beneath the blue-and-gold ceiling like two large, ugly sea creatures. “Come. We must alert the other Heads of House. You’d better put that Cloak back on.”

## Preparing for Defense and The Arrival of Snape

She marched toward the door, and as she did so she raised her wand. From the tip burst three silver cats with spectacle markings around their eyes. The **Patronuses** ran sleekly ahead, filling the spiral staircase with silvery light, as Professor McGonagall, Harry, and Luna hurried back down.

Along the corridors they raced, and one by one the Patronuses left them. Professor McGonagall’s tartan dressing gown rustled over the floor, and Harry and Luna jogged behind her under the Cloak.

They had descended two more floors when another set of quiet joined theirs. Harry, whose scar was still prickling, heard them first. He felt in the pouch around his neck for the **Marauder’s Map**, but before he could take it out, Mc

## Dialogue on Defending Hogwarts

“You realize, of course, that **nothing we do will be able to keep out You-Know-Who indefinitely?**” squeaked **Flitwick**.

“But we can hold him up,” said **Professor Sprout**.

“Thank you, Pomona,” said **Professor McGonagall**, and between the two witches there passed a look of grim understanding.  
“I suggest we establish **basic protection around the place**, then gather our students and meet in the **Great Hall**. Most must be evacuated, though if any of those who are **over age** wish to stay and fight, I think they ought to be given the chance.”

“Agreed,” said Professor Sprout, already hurrying toward the door.  
“I shall meet you in the Great Hall in twenty minutes with my House.”  

And as she jogged out of sight, they could hear her muttering,  
“**Tentacula, Devil’s Snare. And Snargaluff pods…** yes, I’d like to see the Death Eaters fighting those.”

---

## Actions of Professor Flitwick and Discussion of the Ravenclaw Diadem

“I can act from here,” said **Flitwick**, and although he could barely see out of it, he pointed his wand through the smashed window and started muttering **incantations of great complexity**. Harry heard a weird rushing noise, as though Flitwick had unleashed the power of the wind into the grounds.

“Professor,” Harry said, approaching the little Charms master.  
“Professor, I’m sorry to interrupt, but this is important. Have you got any idea where the **diadem of Ravenclaw** is?”

“—**Protego Horribillis**—the diadem of Ravenclaw?” squeaked Flitwick.  
“A little extra wisdom never goes amiss, Potter, but I hardly think it would be much use in this situation!”

“I only meant—do you know where it is? Have you ever seen it?”

“Seen it? **Nobody has seen it in living memory!** Long since lost, my boy!”

Harry felt a mixture of desperate disappointment and panic.  
**What, then, was the Horcrux?**

---

## Preparing the School for Battle

“We shall meet you and your Ravenclaws in the Great Hall, Filius!” said Professor McGonagall, beckoning to Harry and Luna to follow her.

They had just reached the door when **Slughorn** rumbled into speech.

“My word,” he puffed, pale and sweaty, his walrus mustache aquiver.  
“What a to-do! I’m not at all sure whether this is wise, Minerva. He is bound to find a way in, you know, and anyone who has tried to delay him will be in the most grievous peril—”

“I shall expect you and the **Slytherins** in the Great Hall in twenty minutes also,” said Professor McGonagall.  
“If you wish to leave with your students, we shall not stop you. But if any of you attempt to **sabotage our resistance** or take up arms against us within this castle, then, Horace, we duel to kill.”

“Minerva!” he said, aghast.

“The time has come for Slytherin House to decide upon its **loyalties**,” interrupted Professor McGonagall.  
“Go and wake your students, Horace.”

---

## Mobilizing the Castle Defenses

Harry did not stay to watch Slughorn splutter. He and Luna stayed after Professor McGonagall, who had taken up a position in the middle of the corridor and raised her wand.

“**Piertotum—oh, for heaven’s sake, Filch, not now—**”

The aged caretaker had just come hobbling into view, shouting,  
“Students out of bed! Students in the corridors!”

“They’re supposed to be here, you blithering idiot!” shouted McGonagall.  
“Now go and do something constructive! Find Peeves!”

‘P-Peeves?’ stammered Filch as though he had never heard the name before.

“Yes, Peeves, you fool, Peeves! Haven’t you been complaining about him for a quarter of a century?  
Go and fetch him, at once!”

Filch evidently thought Professor McGonagall had taken leave of her senses, but hobbled away, hunch-shouldered, muttering under his breath.

“And now—**Piertotum Locomotor!**” cried Professor McGonagall.  
All along the corridor the **statues and suits of armor** jumped down from their plinths, and from the echoing crashes from the floors above and below, Harry knew that their fellows throughout the castle had done the same.

“Hogwarts is threatened!” shouted Professor McGonagall.  
“Man the boundaries, protect us, do your duty to our school!”

Clattering and yelling, the horde of moving statues stampeded past Harry, some of them smaller, others larger than life.  
There were animals too, and the clanking suits of armor brandished swords and spiked balls on chains.

“Now, Potter,” said Professor McGonagall,  
“you and Miss Lovegood had better return to your friends and bring them to the Great Hall—I shall rouse the other Gryffindors.”

---

## Gathering Allies in the Room of Requirement

They parted at the top of the next staircase, Harry and Luna turning back toward the concealed entrance to the **Room of Requirement**. As they ran, they met crowds of students, most wearing traveling cloaks over their pajamas, being shepherded down to the Great Hall by teachers and prefects.

- “That was Potter!”
- “Harry Potter!”
- “It was him, I swear, I just saw him!”

But Harry did not look back, and at last they reached the entrance to the Room of Requirement.  
Harry leaned against the enchanted wall, which opened to admit them, and he and Luna sped back down the steep staircase.

---

## Rallying the Fighters

“Wh—?”

As the room came into view, Harry slipped down a few stairs in shock.  
It was packed, far more crowded than when he had last been in there.  

Present were:  
- **Kingsley**  
- **Lupin**  
- **Oliver Wood**  
- **Katie Bell**  
- **Angelina Johnson**  
- **Alicia Spinnet**  
- **Bill and Fleur**  
- **Mr. and Mrs. Weasley**

“Harry, what’s happening?” said Lupin, meeting him at the foot of the stairs.

“Voldemort’s on his way, they’re barricading the school—Snape’s run for it—What are you doing here? How did you know?”

“We sent messages to the rest of **

## Evacuation and Student Reactions

**Evacuation** will be overseen by **Mr. Filch** and **Madame Pomfrey**. **Prefects** are instructed to organize their Houses and lead students to the evacuation point in an orderly fashion.

Many students looked **petrified**. As Harry searched the **Gryffindor** table for **Ron** and **Hermione**, **Ernie Macmillan** stood up from the **Hufflepuff** table and shouted, “And what if we want to stay and fight?” This was met with a smattering of applause.

Professor **McGonagall** replied, “If you are of age, you may stay.”

A girl at the **Ravenclaw** table asked about their belongings. McGonagall emphasized, “We have no time to collect possessions. The important thing is to get you out of here safely.” A girl from the **Slytherin** table asked about **Professor Snape**’s whereabouts, and McGonagall replied that he “has done a bunk,” prompting cheers from the other Houses.

## Protection and Voldemort’s Threat

Professor **McGonagall** informed the students that **protection** had been placed around the castle but likely would not hold long. She urged students to move quickly and calmly, following their prefects.

Suddenly, a **high, cold, and clear voice** echoed through the Hall, seemingly from the walls themselves:

- The voice claimed knowledge of the students preparing to fight.
- Declared their efforts **futile** and stated no desire to kill or spill magical blood.
- Demanded **Harry Potter** be handed over to avoid harm.
- Gave a **deadline: midnight**.
  
The Hall fell into an intense silence as all eyes turned to Harry. Then **Pansy Parkinson** from the Slytherin table screamed, urging someone to grab Harry.

## Response of the Houses

- **Gryffindors** stood facing the Slytherins.
- **Hufflepuffs** and **Ravenclaws** followed, all wielding wands.
- Professor McGonagall told **Miss Parkinson** to leave with Mr. Filch first, followed by her House.

Slytherins trooped out, while some older **Ravenclaws, Hufflepuffs,** and about half of **Gryffindor** remained, requiring further instruction to evacuate.

## Battle Plans and Organization

**Kingsley** addressed remaining students:

- Half an hour remained until midnight.
- A **battle plan** had been agreed upon by **Hogwarts teachers** and the **Order of the Phoenix**.
- Professors **Flitwick**, **Sprout**, and **McGonagall** would lead fighters to the castle’s three highest towers: **Ravenclaw**, **Astronomy**, and **Gryffindor**.
- **Remus Lupin**, **Arthur Weasley**, and Kingsley would take groups into the school grounds.
- Defense of entrances and passageways needed organizing, a task taken up by **Fred** and **George** Weasley.

Professor McGonagall urged **Harry** to remember what he was supposed to be looking for.

## Harry’s Search for the Horcrux

Harry, almost forgetting the **Horcrux**, ran out of the Great Hall among evacuating students and up a deserted corridor. He struggled with **fear** and **panic** but tried to concentrate on finding the Horcrux.

Pulling out the **Marauder’s Map**, he noticed neither Ron’s nor Hermione’s names, though the crowd toward the **Room of Requirement** could be concealing them.

Harry reflected that **Voldemort** might expect him to go to **Ravenclaw Tower**.

- **Alecto Carrow** was stationed there by Voldemort.
- Voldemort feared the Horcrux was connected to Ravenclaw, likely the **lost diadem**.
  
Harry considered how Voldemort, a **Slytherin**, could have found the diadem that had eluded generations of Ravenclaws, pondering if someone had told him its location.

## Encounter with Nearly Headless Nick and the Gray Lady

Seeing a **white figure** floating, Harry called to **Nearly Headless Nick**, ghost of Gryffindor Tower.

Harry asked Nick about the **ghost of Ravenclaw Tower**.

- Nick introduced her as the **Gray Lady**.
- The Gray Lady appeared as a tall, proud ghost with waist-length hair and a floor-length cloak.

Harry followed and confronted the Gray Lady, pleading for help to locate the lost diadem.

## The Gray Lady’s Revelation

- The Gray Lady initially refused help, citing numerous previous student requests.
- When pressed about Voldemort, she expressed reluctance but eventually shared her secret.
- She revealed she was **Helena Ravenclaw**, daughter of the original owner of the diadem.
- Helena confessed she had **stolen the diadem** from her mother to make herself cleverer and more important.
  
Harry listened intently, realizing this new information was crucial to defeating Voldemort.

## The Gray Lady’s Story

**The Gray Lady** confessed that her **mother** never admitted the **diadem** was lost and pretended she still had it. She concealed her loss and the betrayal from the other **founders of Hogwarts**.

Her mother eventually fell **fatally ill** but wished to see her one last time. She sent a man who had loved her, though spurned by the Gray Lady, to find her. This man was relentless.

He found her hiding in a **forest** and, when she refused to return, became violent. The man was the **Bloody Baron**, known to be hot-tempered. In a fit of jealousy, he stabbed her.

The Baron was overcome with remorse after stabbing her and used the same weapon to kill himself. He has worn his chains in penitence for centuries.

The **diadem** was hidden inside a **hollow tree** in a forest in **Albania**, a place thought far beyond her mother’s reach.

## How Voldemort Found the Diadem

**Tom Riddle (Voldemort)** learned the location of the diadem from the Gray Lady, likely through charm and manipulation. He traveled to the Albanian forest and retrieved the diadem before beginning work at **Borgin and Burkes**.

The secluded Albanian woods were later likely used by Voldemort to lie low for ten years.

However, the diadem was not left in the tree after becoming a **Horcrux**. Voldemort must have secretly returned it to **Hogwarts Castle** — possibly the night he asked **Dumbledore** for a teaching job.

## The Battle Begins

At **midnight**, the battle at Hogwarts commenced. **Hagrid** arrived dramatically through a broken window, accompanied by **Grawpy** and the boarhound **Fang**. He conveyed the urgency of the situation and the need to fight.

Sounds of battle, flashes of light, and chaos filled the castle corridors. Hagrid joined Harry as they searched for **Ron** and **Hermione**.

## The Castle in Chaos

The first casualties were evident: the two **stone gargoyles** from the staffroom entrance were shattered by a jinx, yet their remains stirred feebly.

Harry was reminded of the **marble bust of Rowena Ravenclaw** and the statue in **Ravenclaw Tower** crowned with a stone diadem.

He also recalled placing a wig and hat on a stone effigy of an ugly old warlock — a secret location known to him and Voldemort but undiscovered by others like **Dumbledore** or **Flitwick**.

## Preparing for Battle

Professor **Sprout**, Neville, and others hurried past with **Mandrakes** in large pots, ready to use them against the attackers.

The castle’s enchantments shook violently; a giant vase exploded off its plinth. Fang fled terrified while Hagrid chased after him, leaving Harry alone.

## Allies and Encounters

The **painted knight Sir Cadrigan** accompanied Harry, cheering him on as he raced through corridors.

Harry met **Fred Weasley**, **Lee Jordan**, **Hannah Abbott**, and others at a hidden passage concealed by a statue’s empty plinth.

Owls fluttered wildly as **Mrs. Norris** tried to manage them amidst the chaos.

Aberforth Dumbledore confronted Harry, questioning the decision to evacuate students without hostage security for **Slytherin** students related to Death Eaters. Harry defended Dumbledore’s honor and decisions.

## Reunion with Ron and Hermione

Harry finally found **Ron** and **Hermione** carrying large curved, dirty yellow objects: **basilisk fangs**.

Ron and Hermione had ventured into the **Chamber of Secrets** to retrieve the fangs, as basilisk teeth could destroy Horcruxes.

Ron demonstrated his ability to speak **Parseltongue**, learned from Harry, which enabled their entry.

Hermione praised Ron’s skill, and Ron modestly credited their success to persistence.

## Destroying Horcruxes

Ron revealed the destruction of **Hufflepuff’s cup**, stabbed by Hermione.

Harry celebrated their victory, acknowledging the importance of the progress against Voldemort.

Suddenly, an explosion rocked the ceiling above, dust fell, and a distant scream echoed, signaling the battle’s escalating danger.

## The Hidden Diadem and the Room of Requirement

“I know what the **diadem** looks like, and I know where it is,” said **Harry**, talking fast. “He hid it exactly where I had my old **Potions book**, where everyone’s been hiding stuff for centuries. He thought he was the only one to find it. Come on.”  

As the walls trembled again, he led the other two back through the concealed entrance and down the staircase into the **Room of Requirement**. It was empty except for three women: **Ginny**, **Tonks**, and an elderly witch wearing a moth-eaten hat, whom Harry recognized immediately as **Neville’s grandmother**.  

“Ah, Potter,” she said crisply as if she had been waiting for him. “You can tell us what’s going on.”  

“Is everyone okay?” said Ginny and Tonks together.  

“’S far as we know,” said Harry. “Are there still people in the passage to the **Hog’s Head**?”  

He knew that the room would not be able to transform while there were still users inside it.  

“I was the last to come through,” said **Mrs. Longbottom**. “I sealed it, I think it unwise to leave it open now **Aberforth** has left his pub. Have you seen my grandson?”  

“He’s fighting,” said Harry.  

“Naturally,” said the old lady proudly. “Excuse me, I must go and assist him.”  

With surprising speed she trotted off toward the stone steps.  

## The Fight and Strategic Movements

Harry looked at Tonks.  

“I thought you were supposed to be with **Teddy** at your mother’s?”  

“I couldn’t stand not knowing—” Tonks looked anguished. “She’ll look after him—have you seen **Remus**?”  

“He was planning to lead a group of fighters into the grounds—”  

Without another word, Tonks sped off.  

“Ginny,” said Harry, “I’m sorry, but we need you to leave too. Just for a bit. Then you can come back in.”  

Ginny looked simply delighted to leave her sanctuary.  

“And then you can come back in!” he shouted after her as she ran up the steps after Tonks. “You’ve got to come back in!”  

“Hang on a moment!” said **Ron** sharply. “We’ve forgotten someone!”  

“Who?” asked **Hermione**.  

“The **house-elves**, they’ll all be down in the kitchen, won’t they?”  

“You mean we ought to get them fighting?” asked Harry.  

“No,” said Ron seriously, “I mean we should tell them to get out. We don’t want anymore Dobbies, do we? We can’t order them to die for us—”  

## A Moment of Lightness Amidst War  

There was a clatter as the **basilisk fangs** cascaded out of Hermione’s arms. Running at Ron, she flung them around his neck and kissed him full on the mouth.  

Ron threw away the fangs and broomstick he was holding and responded with such enthusiasm that he lifted Hermione off her feet.  

“Is this the moment?” Harry asked weakly, and when nothing happened except that Ron and Hermione gripped each other still more firmly and swayed on the spot, he raised his voice.  

“Oi! There’s a war going on here!”  

Ron and Hermione broke apart, their arms still around each other.  

“I know, mate,” said Ron, who looked as though he had recently been hit on the back of the head with a **Bludger**, “so it’s now or never, isn’t it?”  

“Never mind that, what about the **Horcrux**?” Harry shouted. “D’you think you could just—just hold it in until we’ve got the diadem?”  

“Yeah—right—sorry—” said Ron, and he and Hermione set about gathering up fangs, both pink in the face.  

## The Castle is Under Siege

It was clear, as the three of them stepped back into the corridor upstairs, that in the minutes they had spent in the Room of Requirement the situation within the castle had deteriorated severely:  

- The walls and ceiling were shaking worse than ever  
- Dust filled the air  
- Bursts of **green and red light** were close to the foot of the castle, signaling the Death Eaters were near  
- **Grawp the giant** meandered by, swinging what looked like a stone gargoyle torn from the roof and roaring his displeasure  

“Let’s hope he steps on some of them!” said Ron as more screams echoed from close by.  

“As long as it’s not any of our lot!” said a voice: Harry turned and saw Ginny and Tonks, both with their wands drawn at the next window, which was missing several panes. Ginny sent a well-aimed jinx into a crowd of fighters below.  

“Good girl!” roared a figure running through the dust toward them, and Harry saw **Aberforth** again, his gray hair flying as he led a small group of students past.  

“They look like they might be breaching the north battlements, they’ve brought giants of their own.”  

“Have you seen Remus?” Tonks called after him.  

“He was dueling **Dolohov**,” shouted Aberforth, “haven’t seen him since!”  

“Tonks,” said Ginny, “Tonks, I’m sure he’s okay—”  

But Tonks had run off into the dust after Aberforth.  

Ginny turned, helpless, to Harry, Ron, and Hermione.  

“They’ll be all right,” said Harry, though he knew they were empty words. “Ginny, we’ll be back in a moment, just keep out of the way, keep safe—come on!” he said to Ron and Hermione, and they ran back to the stretch of wall beyond which the **Room of Requirement** was waiting to do the bidding of the next entrant.  

## The Room of Hidden Things

“I need the place where everything is hidden.” Harry begged of it inside his head, and the door materialized on their third run past.  

The furor of the battle died the moment they crossed the threshold and closed the door behind them:  

- All was silent  
- They were in a place the size of a cathedral  
- It had the appearance of a city, with towering walls built of objects hidden by thousands of long-gone students  

“And he never realized anyone could get in?” said Ron, his voice echoing in the silence.  

“He thought he was the only one,” said Harry. “Too bad for him I’ve had to hide stuff in my time… this way,” he added. “I think it’s down here…”  

They sped off up adjacent aisles; Harry could hear the others’ footsteps echoing through the towering piles of junk:  

- Bottles  
- Hats  
- Crates  
- Chairs  
- Books  
- Weapons  
- Broomsticks  
- Bats  

“Somewhere near here,” Harry muttered to himself. “Somewhere… somewhere…”  

Deeper and deeper into the labyrinth he went, looking for objects he recognized from his one previous trip into the room. His breath was loud in his ears, and then his very soul seemed to shiver.  

There it was, right ahead: the blistered old cupboard in which he had hidden his old **Potions book**, and on top of it, the pockmarked stone warlock wearing a dusty old wig and what looked like an ancient discolored **tiara**.  

He had already stretched out his hand, though he remained a few feet away, when a voice behind him said, “Hold it, Potter.”  

## Confrontation with Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyle

He skidded to a halt and turned around. **Crabbe** and **Goyle** were standing behind him, shoulder to shoulder, wands pointing right at Harry. Through the small space between their jeering faces he saw **Draco Malfoy**.  

“That’s my wand you’re holding, Potter,” said Malfoy, pointing his own through the gap between Crabbe and Goyle.  

“Not anymore,” panted Harry, tightening his grip on the **hawthorn wand**. “Winners, keepers, Malfoy. Who’s lent you theirs?”  

“My mother,” said Draco.  

Harry laughed, though there was nothing very humorous about the situation. He could not hear Ron or Hermione anymore. They seemed to have run out of earshot, searching for the diadem.  

“So how come you three aren’t with Voldemort?” asked Harry.  

“We’re gonna be rewarded,” said Crabbe. His voice was surprisingly soft for such an enormous person: Harry had hardly ever heard him speak before. Crabbe was speaking like a small child promised a large bag of sweets. “We ’ung back, Potter. We decided not to go. Decided to bring you to ’im.”  

“Good plan,” said Harry in mock admiration. He could not believe that he was this close, and was going to be thwarted by Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyle. He began edging slowly backward toward the place where the Horcrux sat lopsided upon the bust. If he could just get his hands on it before the fight broke out…  

“So how did you get in here?” he asked, trying to distract them.  

“I virtually lived in the **Room of Hidden Things** all last year,” said Malfoy, his voice brittle. “I know how to get in.”  

“We was hiding in the corridor outside,” grunted Goyle. “We can do **Disillusionment Charms** now! And then,” his face split into a gormless grin, “you turned up right in front of us and said you was looking for a die-dum! What’s a die-dum?”  

“Harry?” Ron’s voice echoed suddenly from the other side of the wall to Harry’s right. “Are you talking to someone?”  

## The Battle Intensifies

With a whiplike movement, Crabbe pointed his wand at the fifty-foot mountain of old furniture, broken trunks, books, robes, and unidentifiable junk, and shouted, “**Descendo!**”  

The wall began to totter, then the top third crumbled into the aisle next door where Ron stood.  

“Ron!” Harry bellowed, as somewhere out of sight Hermione screamed, and Harry heard innumerable objects crashing to the floor on the other side of the destabilized wall. He pointed his wand at the rampart, cried, “**Finite!**” and it steadied.  

“No!” shouted Malfoy, staying Crabbe’s arm as the latter made to repeat his spell. “If you wreck the room you might bury this diadem thing!”  

“What’s that matter?” said Crabbe, tugging himself free. “It’s Potter the Dark Lord wants, who cares about a die-dum?”  

“Potter came in here to get it,” said Malfoy with ill-disguised impatience at the slow-wittedness of his colleagues. “So that must mean—”  

“‘Must mean’?” Crabbe turned on Malfoy with undisguised ferocity. “Who cares what you think? I don’t take your orders no more, Draco. You an’ your dad are finished.”  

“Harry?” shouted Ron again, from the other side of the junk wad. “What’s going on?”  

“Harry?” mimicked Crabbe. “What’s going on—no, Potter! **Crucio!**”  

Harry had lunged for the tiara; Crabbe’s curse missed him but hit the stone bust, which flew into the air; the diadem soared upward and then dropped out of sight in the mass of objects on which the bust had rested.  

“STOP!” Malfoy shouted at Crabbe, his voice echoing through the enormous room. “The Dark Lord wants him alive—”  

“So? I’m not killing him, am I?” yelled Crabbe, throwing off Malfoy’s restraining arm. “But if I can, I will, the Dark Lord wants him dead anyway, what’s the diff—?”  

A jet of scarlet light shot past Harry by inches: Hermione had run around the corner behind him and sent a **Stunning Spell** straight at Crabbe’s head. It only missed because Malfoy pulled him out of the way.  

“It’s that Mudblood! **Avada Kedavra!**”  

Harry saw Hermione dive aside, and his fury that Crabbe had aimed to kill wiped all else from his mind. He shot a Stunning Spell at Crabbe, who lurched out of the way, knocking Malfoy’s wand out of his hand; it rolled out of sight beneath a mountain of broken furniture and bones.  

“Don’t kill him! DON’T KILL HIM!” Malfoy yelled at Crabbe and Goyle, who were both aiming at Harry: Their split second’s hesitation was all Harry needed.  

“**Expelliarmus!**”  

Goyle’s wand flew out of his hand and disappeared into the bulwark of objects beside him; Goyle leapt foolishly on the spot, trying to retrieve it; Malfoy jumped out of range of Hermione’s second Stunning Spell, and Ron, appearing suddenly at the end of the aisle, shot a full **Body-Bind Curse** at Crabbe, which narrowly missed.  

Crabbe wheeled around and screamed, “Avada Kedavra!” again. Ron leapt out of sight to avoid the jet of green light. The wandless Malfoy cowered behind a three-legged wardrobe as Hermione charged toward them, hitting Goyle with a Stunning Spell as she came.  

“It’s somewhere here!” Harry yelled at her, pointing at the pile of junk into which the old tiara had fallen. “Look for it while I go and help R—”  

“HARRY!” she screamed.  

## The Flames and Warning  

A roaring, billowing noise behind him gave him a moment’s warning. He turned and saw both Ron and Crabbe running as hard as they could up the aisle toward them.  

“Like it hot, scum?” roared Crabbe as he ran.  

But he seemed to have no control over what he had done. Flames of abnormal size were pursuing them, licking up the sides of the junk bulwarks, which were crumbling to soot at their touch.

## The Fiendfyre in the Room of Requirement

**Harry**, **Ron**, and **Hermione** were pursued by a **cursed fire** conjured by **Crabbe**. The flames were alive, forming **fiery beasts** such as **flaming serpents**, **chimaeras**, and **dragons**, intent on killing them.  

The fire was mutating and feeding on centuries of forbidden magical objects and secrets hidden in the Room of Requirement.

---

### Escape on Broomsticks

- Harry grabbed two broomsticks, throwing one to **Ron**, who helped **Hermione** onboard.  
- They narrowly avoided attacks from fiery beasts as they rose into the air.  
- Below, the cursed fire consumed ancient contraband, evidence of countless banned experiments.  
- Harry searched desperately for **Malfoy**, **Crabbe**, and **Goyle**, but could see nothing but fire.

---

### Rescue Attempt and Flight to Safety

- Harry heard a human scream and spotted **Malfoy** holding an unconscious **Goyle** atop a fragile tower of desks.  
- Harry attempted a rescue, but **Goyle** was too heavy, and Malfoy’s sweaty hand slipped from his grasp.  
- Ron warned Harry, and he, Ron, and Hermione managed to drag Goyle onto their brooms, escaping the flames.  
- Malfoy climbed onto Harry’s broom as they flew toward the door amid swirling smoke.  

---

### The Diadem and Fiendfyre

- Harry caught the falling **diadem**, inscribed with the words:  
  **“WIT BEYOND MEASURE IS MAN’S GREATEST TREASURE.”**  
- The diadem was hot and blackened but began to vibrate and break apart in his hands.  
- Harry thought he heard a faint scream from the breaking object.  
- Hermione explained the fire was **Fiendfyre**, a **cursed fire** capable of destroying **Horcruxes**. Crabbe must have learned its use from the **Carrows**.  

---

## The Battle Continues: Death Eaters Invade Hogwarts

- After escaping the Room, the battle was still raging across Hogwarts.  
- Harry, Ron, and Hermione encountered **Fred** and **Percy** dueling **Death Eaters**.  
- **Percy** fired a jinx at **Thicknesse**, who dropped his wand and writhed in pain, transforming partly into a sea urchin.  
- The group fought valiantly, stunning and transfiguring their opponents.

---

### The Explosion and Aftermath

- Suddenly, the area exploded, throwing Harry into rubble.  
- He was badly injured and bleeding, struggling to stand amid the smashed corridor.  
- He heard a terrible cry and saw **Hermione** struggling to rise.  
- Nearby, **Fred**, **Percy**, and **Ron** were with a fallen figure—Fred lay motionless, his face etched with a final laugh.  

---

## 32. THE ELDER WAND

### Fred’s Death and the Oncoming Danger

- Harry grappled with the horror of **Fred’s death**, feeling disbelief amid the ongoing battle.  
- As curses flew through the hole in the castle wall, Harry, Ron, and Hermione took cover on the floor.  
- **Percy** shielded Fred’s body, refusing to move despite Harry’s urging.  

---

### Giant Spiders Join the Fight

- A monstrous spider, a descendant of **Aragog**, tried to enter through the hole.  
- Harry and Ron’s spells pushed the giant spider back into the darkness.  
- More spiders from the **Forbidden Forest** began climbing the castle walls, summoned by the chaos.  

---

### Evacuating Fred’s Body

- With curses flying overhead, Harry, Ron, Hermione, and Percy cautiously moved Fred’s body out of harm's way.  
- They stayed low to avoid the continuous attacks from Death Eaters and monstrous creatures alike.

## Battle at Hogwarts: The Shrieking Shack and the Final Confrontation

### The Hidden Niche and the Chaos of Battle

- **Harry** was placed in a **niche** where a suit of armor had stood, unable to look longer at **Fred**.
- The corridor was full of **dust**, **falling masonry**, and people running in confusion.
- **Percy** shouted a roar, “ROOKWOOD!” and chased after a tall man pursuing students.

### Hermione’s Intervention

- **Hermione** pulled **Ron** behind a tapestry, struggling to stop him from chasing Percy.
- Ron was filled with rage and grief, desperate to kill **Death Eaters** and help.
- Hermione pleaded, emphasizing that **they were the only ones who could end it** and they needed to focus on finding and destroying the **snake (Horcrux)**.

### Harry's Connection to Voldemort

- Harry’s **scar** burned, urging him to enter Voldemort’s mind.
- He visualized a **desolate, familiar room** inside the castle — the secret room only Harry had found.
- The room was dimly lit with a single oil lamp, muffled sounds of the castle attack outside.

### Voldemort’s Desperation

- **Lucius Malfoy**, wounded and fearful, pleaded about his son and the battle.
- Voldemort dismissed Lucius’s concerns, confident that **Harry Potter** would come to him.
- Voldemort twirled his wand nervously, troubled, and commanded Lucius to fetch **Severus Snape** for a dark service.

### Nagini's Protection and Voldemort’s Strategy

- Voldemort whispered to **Nagini**, his giant snake, kept in a magical **protected sphere**.
- Harry was abruptly pulled back to the battle by sounds of combat.
- He reported that **Voldemort was in the Shrieking Shack with Nagini**, protected magically, and had just sent Lucius to find Snape.

### The Plan to Retrieve the Horcrux

- Hermione was outraged that Voldemort was not fighting directly.
- Harry explained Voldemort expected him to come for the snake, the last **Horcrux**.
- Ron volunteered to retrieve the Horcrux, but Harry insisted on taking the **Invisibility Cloak** himself.

### Attack and Escape Through the Chute

- Two masked **Death Eaters** appeared near the tapestry.
- Hermione cast **Glisseo**, turning the stairs into a chute that sped them down fast.
- At the bottom, Hermione used **Duro** to turn the tapestry to stone, trapping the Death Eaters.

### The Battle in the Corridors

- They encountered numerous duelers: **Death Eaters** versus students and teachers.
- **Dean** and **Parvati** fought bravely against powerful foes.
- **Peeves** aided by dropping **Snargaluff pods**, which exploded with wriggling green tubers on Death Eaters.

### Running Through the Fight Under the Cloak

- They threw the Cloak over themselves to avoid detection.
- Ron was briefly covered with Snargaluff tubers, suspended oddly in midair.
- They made a break toward the marble staircase and the entrance hall.

### Encounter with Draco Malfoy

- **Draco Malfoy** was on the upper landing, pleading with Death Eaters.
- Ron punched Malfoy, saving him and calling him a “two-faced bastard” for the second time that night.
- Death Eaters and fighters filled the stairwell and hall.

### Battle in the Entrance Hall

- **Yaxley** battled **Flitwick**, a masked Death Eater fought **Kingsley**, while students ran with injured friends.
- **Neville** wielded **Venomous Tentacula** to trap a Death Eater.
- The **Slytherin hourglass** spilled emeralds, causing people to slip.

### The Arrival of Fenrir Greyback and Magical Defense

- **Lavender Brown** was attacked by **Fenrir Greyback**.
- Hermione blasted Greyback backward with a deafening spell.
- A **crystal ball** fell on Greyback’s head, knocking him unconscious.
- **Professor Trelawney** threw more crystal spheres as magical projectiles against the invading **giant spiders** entering the hall.

### The Spider Attack and Hagrid’s Intervention

- Spiders swarmed in through the front doors, causing fear among both Death Eaters and defenders.
- **Hagrid** charged down the stairs, shouting, “Don’t hurt ’em, don’t hurt ’em!”
- Harry tried to stop Hagrid but saw him get swallowed by the spiders.
- The spiders retreated as spells rained down with Hagrid caught in their midst.
- Harry and the others cried out, “HAGRID!” in alarm.

## Encounter with the Giant

Harry heard someone calling his name, whether **friend** or **foe** he did not care. He was springing down the front steps into the dark grounds, where **spiders** were swarming away with their prey. He could see nothing of **Hagrid** at all.

**“HAGRID!”**

Harry thought he could make out an **enormous arm** waving from the midst of the spider swarm. As he made to chase after them, his way was impeded by a monumental foot, which made the ground shudder beneath him. He looked up to see a **giant**, twenty feet high, with its head hidden in shadow and treelike, hairy shins illuminated by the castle doors.

With one brutal movement, the giant smashed a massive fist through an **upper window**, and glass rained down upon Harry, forcing him back under the shelter of the doorway.

## The Giants’ Battle

**Hermione** shrieked as she and **Ron** caught up with Harry, gazing upward at the giant trying to seize people through the window above.

**“DON’T!”** Ron yelled, grabbing Hermione’s hand as she raised her wand. **“Stun him and he’ll crush half the castle—”**

At that moment, **Grawp** came lurching around the corner of the castle. Harry realized Grawp was an **undersized giant**. The enormous giant, the attacker, roared and stomped toward Grawp. The two giants launched themselves at each other with the savagery of lions.

Harry roared, **“RUN!”** The night was full of hideous yells and blows as the giants wrestled. Harry seized Hermione’s hand and tore down the steps into the grounds, Ron bringing up the rear. They ran halfway toward the forest when they were brought up short.

## The Arrival of the Dementors

The air around them had frozen. Harry’s breath caught and solidified in his chest as **Dementors** advanced toward the castle. Surrounding fighting sounds became muted, replaced by a silence only Dementors could bring. Harry’s friend **Fred** was gone, and **Hagrid** was surely dying or already dead.

Hermione’s voice called out:

**“Come on, Harry! Patronuses, Harry, come on!”**

Harry raised his wand but felt a dull hopelessness spreading through him. He saw Ron’s silver terrier and Hermione’s otter Patronuses falter and fade. His own wand trembled in his hand, and he almost welcomed the coming oblivion.

Suddenly, a **silver hare, boar, and fox** soared past their heads, causing the Dementors to fall back. **Luna, Ernie, and Seamus** arrived out of the darkness, continuing to cast **Patronuses** beside them.

Luna encouraged Harry:

**“That’s right, Harry... come on think of something happy…”**

Harry’s stag Patronus burst from his wand after his greatest effort. Dementors scattered in earnest, and the night became mild again, though the sounds of battle filled the air.

## Another Giant Attack and Escape

Just as peace seemed to return, another giant came lurching from the forest, brandishing a huge club. Harry shouted:

**“RUN!”**

Everyone scattered, narrowly avoiding the giant’s crushing foot. Ron and Hermione followed Harry, but Luna, Ernie, and Seamus vanished back into the battle.

Ron yelled:

**“Let’s get out of range!”**

The giant swung its club again, bellows echoing across the grounds where **red and green light** burst through the darkness.

## The Whomping Willow and Secret Passage

Harry spotted **The Whomping Willow** and urged, **“Go!”**

He tried to wall up his chaotic thoughts—of **Fred**, **Hagrid**, and those he loved. All had to wait because the only way to end the battle was to reach the **snake** and **Voldemort.**

Ignoring jets of light and crashing waves, Harry ran faster than ever, reaching the great tree first. He skirted the Whomping Willow’s slashing branches, searching the bark for a single knot that would paralyze it.

Ron and Hermione caught up, panting. Ron expressed doubt about entering:

**“How—how’re we going to get in? I can—see the place—if we just had—Crookshanks again—”**

Hermione was breathless and asked:

**“Crookshanks? Are you a wizard, or what?”**

Ron cast **Wingardium Leviosa** on a twig, which jabbed near the roots of the tree. The writhing Willow became still.

**“Perfect!”** Hermione panted.

Harry hesitated briefly, thinking that Voldemort might be leading them into a trap. But he knew the truth: the only way forward was to kill the snake, located where Voldemort was, at the tunnel’s end.

Ron urged:

**“Harry, we’re coming, just get in there!”**

Harry wriggled into the earthy passage hidden among the tree’s roots. The tunnel was a tight squeeze and low-ceilinged, forcing them to crawl silently, Harry’s wand illuminating the path ahead.

At last, the tunnel sloped upward, and Harry saw a sliver of light. Hermione whispered:

**“The Cloak! Put the Cloak on!”**

Harry drew the slippery cloth over himself, murmured **“Nox”** to extinguish his wand light, and crawled on, senses straining to avoid detection.

## Spying on Voldemort and Snape

Voices drifted from the room ahead, muffled by an old crate blocking the tunnel’s opening. Harry edged closer and peered through a tiny gap.

In the dimly lit room, Harry saw **Nagini** swirling and coiling like a serpent underwater, encased in an **enchanted, starry sphere** floating unsupported.

A **long-fingered white hand** toyed with a wand.

**Snape** spoke:

**“…my Lord, their resistance is crumbling—”**

**Voldemort** replied, his voice high and clear:

**“—and it is doing so without your help. Skilled wizard though you are, Severus, I do not think you will make much difference now. We are almost there… almost.”**

Snape insisted:

**“Let me find the boy. Let me bring you Potter. I know I can find him, my Lord. Please.”**

Snape passed the gap. Harry kept his eyes on Nagini, wondering if any spell could penetrate the protection without revealing his position.

Voldemort stood, revealing his **red eyes**, **flattened serpentine face**, and pale complexion gleaming in semi-darkness.

He said softly:

**“I have a problem, Severus.”**

Snape responded:

**“My Lord?”**

Voldemort raised the **Elder Wand**, holding it like a conductor’s baton.

**“Why doesn’t it work for me, Severus?”**

There was a faint hiss from the snake, or perhaps Voldemort’s sibilant sigh.

Snape said blankly:

**“My—my lord? I do not understand. You—you have performed extraordinary magic with that wand.”**

Voldemort corrected him:

**“No. I have performed my usual magic. I am extraordinary, but this wand… no. It has not revealed the wonders it has promised. I feel no difference between this wand and the one I procured from Ollivander all those years ago.”**

His tone was calm, but Harry’s scar throbbed with pain and he sensed fury building inside Voldemort.

**“No difference,”** Voldemort repeated.

Snape did not reply. Harry wondered if Snape sensed danger and was searching for the right words to reassure his master.

Voldemort paced while speaking measuredly as pain and fury worsened.

**“I have thought long and hard, Severus… do you know why I have called you back from battle?”**

Harry saw Snape’s profile; his eyes fixed upon the coiling snake in its cage.

Snape begged:

**“No, my Lord, but I beg you will let me return. Let me find Potter.”**

Voldemort said:

**“You sound like Lucius. Neither of you understands Potter as I do. He does not need finding. Potter will come to me. I knew his weakness, you see, his one great flaw. He will hate watching the others struck down around him, knowing that it is for him that it happens. He will want to stop it at any cost. He will come.”**

Snape warned:

**“But my Lord, he might be killed accidentally by someone other than yourself—”**

Voldemort replied:

**“My instructions to the Death Eaters have been perfectly clear. Capture Potter. Kill his friends—the more, the better—but do not kill him.**

**“But it is of you that I wished to speak, Severus, not Harry Potter. You have been very valuable to me. Very valuable.”**

## Snape’s Plea and Voldemort’s Frustration

“My Lord knows I seek only to serve him. But—let me go and find the boy, my Lord. Let me bring him to you. I know I can—”

“I have told you, no!” said **Voldemort**, and Harry caught the glint of red in his eyes as he turned again. The swishing of his cloak was like the slithering of a snake, and he felt Voldemort’s impatience in his burning scar. “My concern at the moment, **Severus**, is what will happen when I finally meet the boy!”

“My Lord, there can be no question, surely—?”

“—but there is a question, Severus. There is.”

Voldemort halted, and Harry could see him plainly again as he slid the **Elder Wand** through his white fingers, staring at Snape.

“Why did both the wands I have used fail when directed at **Harry Potter**?”

“I—I cannot answer that, my Lord.”

“Can’t you?”

The stab of rage felt like a spike driven through Harry’s head; he forced his own fist into his mouth to stop himself from crying out in pain. He closed his eyes, and suddenly he was Voldemort, looking into Snape’s pale face.

“My wand of yew did everything of which I asked it, Severus, except to kill Harry Potter. Twice it failed. Ollivander told me under torture of the twin cores, told me to take another’s wand. I did so, but Lucius’s wand shattered upon meeting Potter’s.”

“I—I have no explanation, my Lord.”

Snape was not looking at Voldemort now. His dark eyes were still fixed upon the coiling serpent in its protective sphere.

---

## The Elder Wand and Its True Master

“I sought a third wand, Severus. The **Elder Wand**, the **Wand of Destiny**, the **Deathstick**. I took it from its previous master. I took it from the grave of **Albus Dumbledore**.”

Now Snape looked at Voldemort, his face like a death mask—marble white and so still that when he spoke, it was a shock to see life behind the blank eyes.

“My Lord—let me go to the boy—”

“All this long night when I am on the brink of victory, I have sat here,” said Voldemort, voice barely louder than a whisper, “wondering why the **Elder Wand** refuses to perform as legend says it must for its rightful owner… and I think I have the answer.”

Snape did not speak.

“Perhaps you already know it? You are a clever man, after all, Severus. You have been a good and faithful servant, and I regret what must happen.”

“My Lord—”

“The Elder Wand cannot serve me properly, Severus, because I am **not its true master**. The Elder Wand belongs to the wizard who **killed its last owner**. You killed Albus Dumbledore. While you live, Severus, the Elder Wand cannot truly be mine.”

“My Lord!” Snape protested, raising his wand.

“It cannot be any other way,” said Voldemort. “I must master the wand, Severus. Master the wand, and I master Potter at last.”

---

## Snape’s Death

Voldemort swiped the air with the Elder Wand. It did nothing to Snape, who seemed briefly reprieved: but then Voldemort’s intention became clear. The snake’s cage rolled through the air, and before Snape could do more than yell, it encased him, head and shoulders. Voldemort spoke in **Parseltongue**.

“Kill.”

A terrible scream followed. Harry saw Snape’s face lose what little color it had; it whitened as his black eyes widened, as the snake’s fangs pierced his neck. He failed to push the enchanted cage off himself, his knees gave way, and he fell to the floor.

“I regret it,” said Voldemort coldly.

He turned away without sadness or remorse. It was time to leave this shack and take charge, with a wand that would now do his full bidding. He pointed it at the starry cage holding the snake, which drifted upward, off Snape, who fell sideways onto the floor, blood gushing from his neck wounds. Voldemort swept away without a backward glance; the great serpent floated after him.

---

## Harry’s Quiet Rescue and Snape’s Last Moments

Back in the tunnel and his own mind, Harry opened his eyes; he had drawn blood biting down on knuckles to stop himself from shouting. Now he watched through a crack, seeing a foot in a black boot trembling on the floor.

“Harry!” breathed **Hermione** behind him, but he had already pointed his wand at the crate blocking his view. It lifted silently and drifted sideways. Quietly, he pulled himself into the room.

He did not know why he was approaching the dying man, nor what he felt seeing Snape’s white face and fingers trying to staunch the bleeding neck wound. Harry took off the **Invisibility Cloak** and looked down upon the man he hated. Snape’s widening black eyes found Harry as he tried to speak.

A terrible rasping, gurgling noise issued from Snape’s throat.

“Take… it… Take… it…”

Something more than blood leaked from Snape: silvery blue, neither gas nor liquid, gushing from his mouth, ears, and eyes. Harry knew what it was, but did not know what to do.

A flask, conjured from thin air, was thrust into Harry’s shaking hand by Hermione. Harry lifted the silvery substance into it with his wand. When the flask was full to the brim and Snape looked as though no blood was left in him, his grip slackened.

“Look… at… me…” he whispered.

The green eyes found the black, but after a second, something in the dark eyes vanished, leaving them fixed, blank, and empty. The hand holding Harry thudded to the floor, and Snape moved no more.

---

## 33. THE PRINCE’S TALE

Harry remained kneeling beside Snape until a high, cold voice spoke so close he jumped, gripping the flask tightly, thinking **Voldemort** had returned.

Voldemort’s voice echoed through the walls and floor, addressing **Hogwarts** and the surrounding area. Residents of **Hogsmeade** and those still fighting would hear him as clearly as if he stood beside them.

“You have fought valiantly. Lord Voldemort knows how to value bravery.

Yet you have sustained heavy losses. If you continue to resist me, you will all die, one by one. I do not wish this to happen. Every drop of magical blood spilled is a loss and a waste.

Lord Voldemort is merciful. I command my forces to **retreat immediately**.

You have one hour. Dispose of your dead with dignity. Treat your injured.

I speak now, **Harry Potter**, directly to you. You have permitted your friends to die for you rather than face me yourself. I shall wait for one hour in the **Forbidden Forest**. If, at the end of that hour, you have not come to me, not given yourself up, then battle recommences. This time, I shall enter the fray myself, Harry Potter, and I shall punish every last man, woman, and child who has tried to conceal you from me. One hour.”

---

## After Voldemort’s Ultimatum

Both **Ron** and **Hermione** shook their heads frantically, looking at Harry.

“Don’t listen to him,” said Ron.

“It’ll be all right,” said Hermione wildly. “Let’s—let’s get back to the castle. If he’s gone to the forest, we’ll need a new plan—”

She glanced at Snape’s body, then hurried back to the tunnel entrance. Ron followed.

Harry gathered the **Invisibility Cloak** and looked down at Snape, feeling shock at both the manner and reason for Snape’s killing.

The three crawled back through the tunnel silently. Harry wondered if Ron and Hermione still heard Voldemort ringing in their heads as he did.

**You have permitted your friends to die for you rather than face me yourself. I shall wait for one hour in the Forbidden Forest… One hour…**

---

## The Aftermath at Hogwarts

Small bundles littered the lawn in front of the castle. It was pitch-black despite being close to dawn. The three hurried toward the stone steps.

A lone dog, as large as a small boat, lay abandoned. There was no sign of **Grawp** or his attacker.

The castle was unnaturally silent. There were no flashes of light, bangs, screams, or shouts. The entrance hall flagged stones were stained with blood. Emeralds, pieces of marble, and splintered wood littered the floor. Part of the banisters had been blown away.

“Where is everyone?” whispered Hermione.

Ron led the way to the **Great Hall**. Harry stopped in the doorway.

The House tables were gone, crowded now with survivors standing in groups, arms around each other's necks. The injured were being treated by **Madam Pomfrey** and helpers on the raised platform. **Firenze** was among the injured, blood pouring from his flank, shaking, unable to stand.

The dead lay in a row in the middle of the Hall. Harry could not see **Fred’s** body, hidden by his family. **George** knelt at his head; **Mrs. Weasley** lay across Fred’s chest, shaking. **Mr. Weasley** stroked her hair, tears cascading down his cheeks.

Ron and Hermione silently walked away. Hermione hugged **Ginny**, whose face was swollen and blotchy. Ron joined **Bill**, **Fleur**, and **Percy**, who put an arm around Ron’s shoulders. As Ginny and Hermione moved closer to the family, Harry had a clear view of the bodies beside Fred: **Remus** and **Tonks**, pale, still, peaceful, apparently asleep beneath the dark enchanted ceiling.

The Great Hall seemed to shrink as Harry reeled backward, unable to draw breath or bear to look at the bodies. He could not face joining the Weasleys, or look into their eyes, knowing Fred might not have died had Harry surrendered.

He turned away and ran up the marble staircase. Lupin, Tonks… he yearned not to feel. He wished he could rip out his heart and everything screaming inside him.

---

## Harry’s Solitude and the Pensieve

The castle was completely empty; even the ghosts seemed to have joined the mourning in the Great Hall. Harry ran without stopping, clutching the crystal flask of Snape’s last memories.

He did not slow until he reached the stone gargoyle guarding the **Headmaster’s office**.

“Password?”

“Dumbledore!” said Harry without thinking, yearning to see him. The gargoyle slid aside, revealing the spiral staircase behind.

But inside the circular office, he found a change. The portraits that lined the walls were empty. No headmasters or headmistresses remained; all had flitted away, charging through paintings around the castle to watch from a distance.

Harry glanced hopelessly at **Dumbledore’s deserted frame**, hanging behind the headmaster’s chair, then turned his back.

The stone **Pensieve** lay in the cabinet as always. Harry heaved it onto the desk and poured Snape’s memories into its wide basin, marked with runes.

To escape into someone else’s thoughts would be a blessed relief. Nothing even Snape left him could be worse than his own.

The memories swirled, silver-white and strange. Without hesitating, with reckless abandonment to assuage his torturing grief, Harry dived in.

## Scene 1: The Playground Encounter

He fell headlong into **sunlight**, and his feet found **warm ground**. When he straightened up, he saw that he was in a nearly **deserted playground**. A single huge **chimney** dominated the distant skyline. Two girls were swinging backward and forward, and a skinny boy was watching them from behind a clump of bushes. His **black hair** was overlong and his clothes were so mismatched that it looked deliberate: too short jeans, a shabby, overlarge coat that might have belonged to a grown man, an odd smocklike shirt.

**Harry** moved closer to the boy. **Snape** looked no more than nine or ten years old, sallow, small, stringy. There was undisguised **greed** in his thin face as he watched the younger of the two girls swinging higher and higher than her sister.

“**Lily, don’t do it!**” shrieked the elder of the two.

But the girl had let go of the swing at the very height of its arc and flown into the air, quite literally **flown**, launched herself skyward with a great shout of **laughter**, and instead of crumpling on the playground asphalt, she soared like a trapeze artist through the air, staying up far too long, landing far too lightly.

“**Mummy told you not to!**”

Petunia stopped her swing by dragging the heels of her sandals on the ground, making a crunching, grinding sound, then leapt up, hands on hips.

“**Mummy said you weren’t allowed, Lily!**”

“But I’m fine,” said Lily, still giggling. “Tuney, look at this. Watch what I can do.”

Petunia glanced around. The playground was deserted apart from themselves and, though the girls did not know it, **Snape**. Lily had picked up a fallen flower from the bush behind which Snape lurked. Petunia advanced, evidently torn between curiosity and disapproval. Lily waited until Petunia was near enough to have a clear view, then held out her palm. The flower sat there, **opening and closing its petals**, like some bizarre, many-lipped oyster.

“**Stop it!**” shrieked Petunia.

“It’s not hurting you,” said Lily, but she closed her hand on the blossom and threw it back to the ground.

“It’s not right,” said Petunia, but her eyes had followed the flower’s flight to the ground and lingered upon it. “**How do you do it?**” she added, and there was definite longing in her voice.

“It’s obvious, isn’t it?” Snape could no longer contain himself, but had jumped out from behind the bushes. Petunia shrieked and ran backward toward the swings, but Lily, though clearly startled, remained where she was. Snape seemed to regret his appearance. A dull flush of color mounted the sallow cheeks as he looked at Lily.

“**What’s obvious?**” asked Lily.

Snape had an air of nervous excitement. With a glance at the distant Petunia, now hovering beside the swings, he lowered his voice and said, “**I know what you are.**”

“**What do you mean?**”

“**You’re… you’re a witch,**” whispered Snape.

She looked affronted.

“**That’s not a very nice thing to say to somebody!**”

She turned, nose in the air, and marched off toward her sister.

“**No!**” said Snape. He was highly colored now, and Harry wondered why he did not take off the ridiculously large coat, unless it was because he did not want to reveal the smock beneath it. He flapped after the girls, looking ludicrously batlike, like his older self.

The sisters considered him, united in disapproval, both holding on to one of the swing poles, as though it was the safe place in tag.

“**You are,**” said Snape to Lily. “You are a witch. I’ve been watching you for a while. But there’s nothing wrong with that. My mum’s one, and I’m a **wizard**.”

Petunia’s laugh was like cold water.
